201507	15	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201507	16	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Lorie and I will again be splitting the Desk briefing in two parts: I will first discuss financial market developments, and Lorie will then discuss Desk operations and balance sheet developments.	61	6
201507	17	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The intermeeting period was characterized by pronounced shifts in risk sentiment and bouts of volatility in some overseas markets largely driven by events in Greece and China.	61	6
201507	18	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	However, volatility in domestic financial markets was not unusually large.	61	6
201507	19	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The top-left panel of your first exhibit shows important events over the intermeeting period, marked with dashed lines.	61	6
201507	20	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The June FOMC statement and SEP release, line 1, resulted in a slight decline in Treasury yields and was largely overshadowed by developments in Greece and China, lines 2 through 5.	61	6
201507	21	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	On net, both equity prices and longer-dated Treasury yields were relatively little changed over the period.	61	6
201507	22	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Treasury yields generally fell on days featuring FOMC communications or top- tier domestic economic data releases, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201507	23	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Market participants highlighted the downward shift in the June SEP “dots” and below- expectations inflation, employment, and retail sales data as main factors driving the declines.	61	6
201507	24	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	In contrast, yields increased, on net, other than in these days, as captured by the “other” category.	61	6
201507	25	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	This category includes days when developments abroad were the main focus.	61	6
201507	26	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Domestic monetary policy communications and data, along with overseas developments, shifted the perceived balance of risks toward a slightly later liftoff.	61	6
201507	27	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	While, on average, respondents to the Desk’s dealer and buy-side surveys attach the highest odds to liftoff occurring in September, as shown in the middle-left panel, the average probability assigned to this outcome declined slightly from the June surveys.	61	6
201507	28	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The associated increase in the odds placed on a later liftoff was spread roughly evenly across future meetings, and the average probability of liftoff is now more than 20 percent for both the December meeting and for meetings thereafter.	61	6
201507	29	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	A small number of Desk survey respondents noted that the potential for strained year-end liquidity conditions might make the Committee reluctant to lift off in December.	61	6
201507	30	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The survey probability of a September liftoff is generally in line with probabilities implied by market prices, shown in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201507	31	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	These probabilities, derived from federal funds futures contracts, declined following the June FOMC events and were then, on net, little changed over the remainder of the period.	61	6
201507	32	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Of course, backing out physical probabilities from market prices is a highly imperfect endeavor and requires numerous assumptions.	61	6
201507	33	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	In addition, one now needs to make an assumption about where market participants believe the effective federal funds rate will trade in the target range.	61	6
201507	34	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The dark blue line in the panel uses the median expectation of 10 basis points above the bottom of the range from a question in the Desk surveys, while the light blue lines use the interquartile range of these expectations.	61	6
201507	35	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The shaded region is based on the full set of responses to the Desk surveys, reflecting a possible range of probabilities that may be drawn from market prices.	61	6
201507	36	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Market participants generally continue to believe the pace of tightening will be gradual, in line with recent communications from Federal Reserve officials.	61	6
201507	37	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Thomas will discuss this more in his briefing.	61	6
201507	38	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	One factor contributing to the gradual expected pace of tightening has been subdued readings of realized inflation.	61	6
201507	39	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Market-based measures of forward inflation remain notably below longer-run historical averages, as shown in the bottom-left panel, though they have increased somewhat since the start of the year as energy prices bottomed out and inflation readings stabilized.	61	6
201507	40	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Over this intermeeting period, forward inflation measures remained relatively steady despite a decline of 14 percent in front-month Brent crude oil futures, in contrast to the highly correlated moves seen over the past year.	61	6
201507	41	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Longer-dated oil futures also declined.	61	6
201507	42	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The recent drop in oil prices appears to have been partly driven both by higher-than-expected supply from Saudi Arabia and Iraq and by expectations for increased supply from Iran over the longer run after an agreement with major international powers cleared the way for sanctions to be lifted.	61	6
201507	43	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The decline in oil prices caused high-yield corporate credit spreads for energy-related firms to increase over the period.	61	6
201507	44	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Credit spreads outside the high-yield energy sector also widened somewhat.	61	6
201507	45	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Yields on benchmark Puerto Rico general obligation bonds also rose sharply, as shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201507	46	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	This occurred after the Puerto Rican government indicated that its public debt burden was unsustainable and that significant concessions from its creditors would be necessary.	61	6
201507	47	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The panel also shows that spillover to other municipal markets has thus far been limited.	61	6
201507	48	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	As discussed in one of your boxes in Tealbook A, risks associated with Puerto Rico at present appear manageable but warrant continued monitoring.	61	6
201507	49	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Turning to your next exhibit, the top-left panel shows that the DXY dollar index increased 2 percent during the period.	61	6
201507	50	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The dollar initially appreciated as investors focused on risks from the euro area and China and, more recently, from the ongoing backdrop of monetary policy divergence across major economies.	61	6
201507	51	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Dollar strength and concerns over Chinese economic growth reportedly contributed to declines in industrial metals prices and commodity-linked currencies over the period.	61	6
201507	52	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The Bloomberg industrial metals index fell nearly 8 percent and developed economy commodity-sensitive currencies, including the Australian and Canadian dollars as well as the Norwegian krone, depreciated an average of 6 percent against the dollar.	61	6
201507	53	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Some market participants suggested that commodity price declines for industrial metals were exacerbated by the sharp fall in Chinese equity prices through a financing linkage.	61	6
201507	54	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	These commodities had reportedly been used by some as collateral to obtain margin financing and were subsequently sold to meet margin calls amid the equity market declines.	61	6
201507	55	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The Shanghai Composite index declined roughly 17 percent over the period, as shown in the top-right panel, and, after taking into account the past two days, is down almost 30 percent from its peak.	61	6
201507	56	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	This peak represented a 150 percent increase since last July.	61	6
201507	57	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	As I discussed at the June meeting, conventional easing measures by the PBOC against a backdrop of slowing mainland economic growth were cited as the primary driver behind the equity market increase over the past 12 months.	61	6
201507	58	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Such easing measures, denoted by the gold diamonds in the chart, included cuts to benchmark interest rates and targeted required reserve ratios.	61	6
201507	59	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	These measures supported the already prevalent use of margin and increase in equity market valuations.	61	6
201507	60	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	However, this dynamic appeared to reverse, and substantial additional conventional easing measures by the PBOC failed to arrest a rapid decline in stock prices in late June.	61	6
201507	61	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	In response, Chinese officials implemented an unprecedented array of measures to halt the sharp correction over the intermeeting period.	61	6
201507	62	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Authorities announced new targeted initiatives on a nearly daily basis, including easing margin trading and collateral requirements, establishing an official stabilization fund to support the equity market, and suspending IPOs.	61	6
201507	63	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	In addition, many firms requested that trading in their shares be halted as a result of the volatility.	61	6
201507	64	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Market participants noted these measures increased “moral hazard” and suggested they may undermine previous market reform efforts.	61	6
201507	65	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Because it is only a  small subset of the Chinese population that invests in mainland equities, market participants believe the correction is unlikely to have a material direct effect on the Chinese economic growth outlook or on asset prices outside China.	61	6
201507	66	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	However, there were a few days over the intermeeting period when negative risk sentiment from Chinese equity price declines spilled over into major global financial markets, especially to other Asian markets.	61	6
201507	67	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Some market participants speculated that this spillover may have reflected concern about a broader loss of control in other parts of the Chinese economy or financial system, in view of the difficulty mainland authorities had stabilizing their equity markets.	61	6
201507	68	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The effects of the Chinese equity market declines were also evident in offshore renminbi currency markets, as some suggested policymakers could also weaken the currency to support domestic export-oriented firms.	61	6
201507	69	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Recall that the renminbi has been appreciating, along with the dollar, against most other currencies for around one year.	61	6
201507	70	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Offshore forward prices and currency option-implied skew reflected increased demand to protect against renminbi depreciation after the peak in Chinese equity prices, as shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201507	71	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	However, these moves were small compared with the changes seen in late 2014 and early 2015, when Chinese officials unexpectedly cut benchmark interest rates and reportedly intervened to stem the extent of the currency depreciation.	61	6
201507	72	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Despite the recent moves in the offshore market and large stock market fluctuations, the onshore renminbi remained remarkably stable.	61	6
201507	73	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The sharp Chinese equity market moves resulted in an average intraday trading range that was more than 4 standard deviations above its typical level since 2000, as shown in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201507	74	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Overall, the recent movements in Chinese equity prices refocused market attention toward risks emanating from the mainland.	61	6
201507	75	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Many participants suggested that the risk of a sharp slowdown in China was of much greater concern than risks stemming from the situation in Greece.	61	6
201507	76	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Steve Kamin will discuss developments in both China and Greece in his briefing.	61	6
201507	77	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Greek developments contributed to elevated realized volatility in euro-area markets, with the intraday trading range of the Italian 10-year yield increasing to its highest level since mid-2013, also shown in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201507	78	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Volatility early in the period was due to uncertainty about the implications of an unraveling of Greek debt negotiations and the “no” vote on the Greek referendum.	61	6
201507	79	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The uncertainty reduced substantially as Greece and its creditors agreed to a temporary bailout package.	61	6
201507	80	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Despite the drama, the knock-on effects across European and global financial markets were relatively contained.	61	6
201507	81	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the bottom-left panel, Greek 10-year debt spreads to Germany widened out substantially, but other peripheral spreads were comparatively little changed, especially relative to their widening in 2011 and 2012.	61	6
201507	82	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Contacts attributed the relatively limited contagion to strengthened financial backstops for other peripheral economies and reduced exposure of core euro-area banks to Greece.	61	6
201507	83	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	In addition, market participants cited expectations that the ECB would use its purchase programs to lean against any significant widening in euro-area peripheral debt spreads or tightening in euro-area financial conditions should the Greek situation deteriorate.	61	6
201507	84	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Increased uncertainty in the euro area also had a very limited effect on domestic bank asset prices, whose behavior Nellie will discuss in her briefing.	61	6
201507	85	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Consistent with the relatively muted response in broader asset prices, the euro has only modestly depreciated 2 percent since the Greek referendum was called.	61	6
201507	86	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Other asset prices sensitive to the macro outlook in Europe, such as the five-year, five-year forward inflation swap rate, were also little influenced by Greek developments, as shown in the bottom-right panel, and remain higher since ECB asset purchases were announced.	61	6
201507	87	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The passage of significant Greek event risks has shifted market attention back to underlying European economic fundamentals, including the fact that forward inflation compensation measures still remain below the ECB’s 2 percent objective.	61	6
201507	88	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	This has caused many to refocus on the theme of the policy divergence consisting of the ECB’s continued easing and the Federal Reserve’s approaching normalization.	61	6
201507	89	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	Lorie will now continue the Desk briefing.	61	6
201507	90	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Thank you, Simon.	61	6
201507	91	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	I will start on exhibit 3 with an update on the swap lines, as we have seen a modest rise in demand from the ECB related to the Greek risk events that Simon discussed.	61	6
201507	92	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-left panel, demand at the ECB’s seven-day dollar auctions reached about $660 million in mid-July.	61	6
201507	93	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Market pricing indicators, however, show no evidence of broad disruption in offshore dollar funding markets.	61	6
201507	94	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	And even if a resurgence of the Greek crisis were to generate more pronounced spillovers in euro- area markets, demand is not likely to return to the much higher levels seen in earlier phases of stress.	61	6
201507	95	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	This is in part due to the financial backstops that now exist in the euro area, but also because euro-area banks have reduced their balance sheets and the associated need for dollar funding compared with previous years.	61	6
201507	96	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	In terms of demand from the BOJ, take-up at the BOJ dollar auctions has been minimal, with the exception of some draws in the seven-day auctions that span quarter-end dates, when market pricing for US dollar funding via one-week FX swaps has notably exceeded the BOJ’s auction rate.	61	6
201507	97	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-right panel, we also continue to see quarter-end volatility in US money market rates, mainly reflecting banks shrinking their balance sheets or requiring a higher return for intermediation in response to incentives arising from regulation.	61	6
201507	98	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	At the June quarter-end, the upward pressure on interdealer repo rates and downward pressure on unsecured rates were broadly consistent with expectations.	61	6
201507	99	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Outside quarter-end, secured and unsecured rates were generally stable over the period, with the ON RRPs continuing to form a soft floor beneath money market rates.	61	6
201507	100	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Reverse repo operations conducted by the Desk proceeded smoothly over the intermeeting period.	61	6
201507	101	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	In addition to its overnight operation, the Desk conducted two term operations over the June quarter-end, the results of which are detailed in your middle-left panel.	61	6
201507	102	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The results were generally as expected, with each of the two offerings modestly oversubscribed.	61	6
201507	103	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The maximum offering rate for the June quarter- end term operations—at 3 basis points above the ON RRP rate—was lower than the 5 basis points over the ON RRP rate that was offered in March.	61	6
201507	104	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	However, the tenors of the term operations were shorter, and the attractiveness of the shorter tenors appeared to offset any effect of the lower rate.	61	6
201507	105	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	These results could suggest that quarter-end term RRP participation was primarily driven by counterparties’ desire to secure investment over the quarter-end, with the desire for incremental yield playing a secondary role.	61	6
201507	106	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	While the Desk’s term operations were fully subscribed, ample capacity remained in the overnight operation over the June quarter-end date.	61	6
201507	107	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Recall that our communication at the time of the June quarter-end term operations took a different approach than in prior quarter-ends in that it separated the announcement of the term RRP offering size and tenor, which was released following the April minutes, from information on the offering rate and other details, which were released following the June FOMC meeting.	61	6
201507	108	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	This strategy allowed us to retain some flexibility to adjust the specific parameters of the operations in case the Committee decided to lift off at the June meeting.	61	6
201507	109	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	This communications change caused little market reaction, and we propose continuing with this practice for the September quarter-end.	61	6
201507	110	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	As summarized in the middle-right panel, we intend to release a statement shortly after the July minutes announcing a plan to offer at least $200 billion in term RRPs at tenors of seven and two days in addition to the $300 billion in ON RRP capacity over the September quarter-end.	61	6
201507	111	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Further, the statement would note that the Desk will release the remaining details of the term RRP operations after the September FOMC event and shortly ahead of quarter-end.	61	6
201507	112	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	We would then come back to the Committee at or shortly after the September meeting with a recommendation for the exact size and maximum offering rate for each operation.	61	6
201507	113	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Looking ahead to other upcoming operational testing, the staff recommends that a series of TDF test operations be held in August.	61	6
201507	114	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The parameters would mirror those of the May series, which included one 14-day and one 7-day operation priced at 1 basis point above IOER.	61	6
201507	115	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Recall that in the spring, the Federal Reserve announced plans to continue TDF testing periodically in order to maintain operational readiness.	61	6
201507	116	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Outside the June quarter-end, daily ON RRP take-up was generally consistent with levels prevailing over prior periods, as shown in the bottom-left panel.	61	6
201507	117	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Federal Reserve repurchase agreements with foreign official institutions—the foreign RP pool—also remained steady at around $150 billion.	61	6
201507	118	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Recall that the foreign RP pool is an overnight investment facility that since the mid-1970s has provided foreign official institution account holders at the Federal Reserve Bank of New York with access to a safe and liquid dollar instrument.	61	6
201507	119	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The investments in the foreign RP pool drain reserves from the System on an overnight basis.	61	6
201507	120	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The size of the foreign RP pool remains notably above its pre-crisis levels, in part reflecting central banks’ desire to hold greater dollar liquidity buffers and a tightening of their counterparty risk- management frameworks following the crisis.	61	6
201507	121	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	It is against this backdrop that I would like to highlight ongoing work to update the foreign RP pool framework, as described in the staff memo circulated in advance of the meeting and summarized in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201507	122	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Historically, we have relied on individual account targets to manage the pool’s aggregate size and daily volatility.	61	6
201507	123	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	However, reflecting the current high-reserve environment, we have informally relaxed account-level targets over the past few years.	61	6
201507	124	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Awareness of this shift among account holders has been uneven because it has not been reflected in their terms of service.	61	6
201507	125	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	To formalize the change in practice and provide clearer communication to customers, the staff intends to revise customer terms of service to remove both individual targets and the requirement to notify the Federal Reserve Bank of New York ahead of balance changes in excess of $100 million.	61	6
201507	126	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	We would establish an internal process for processing individual customer balances above $30 billion, partly for operational reasons and partly to understand the source of the demand.	61	6
201507	127	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	In addition to the benefits associated with improving our communications to customers, these changes would likely increase customer access to high-quality short-term dollar investments at a time when the availability or attractiveness of alternative options in the open market—namely, Treasury bills and commercial bank deposits—may be more limited.	61	6
201507	128	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	As the outlook for excess reserves is not expected to change significantly in the near term, the staff does not expect this to have a material effect on monetary policy implementation.	61	6
201507	129	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	In the event that the size or volatility of the foreign RP pool begins to exert an unwanted influence on money markets, the staff could reintroduce individual targets or caps, or an overall cap.	61	6
201507	130	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The revised terms of service will continue to provide the Federal Reserve with full discretion to make such changes at any time.	61	6
201507	131	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Although take-up in ON RRP operations and usage of the foreign RP pool have remained relatively steady, demand could increase in the near term because of shifts in Treasury bill supply.	61	6
201507	132	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-left panel of your final exhibit, the risk of the debt ceiling binding later this year may lead the Treasury to reduce the supply of bills.	61	6
201507	133	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Indeed, according to Board staff projections, bill supply is expected to decline roughly $90 billion (or 6 percent of total bills outstanding) from current levels through the end of November, around which time the debt ceiling is assumed to be lifted and bill issuance resumed.	61	6
201507	134	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Nonetheless, such a decline in bill supply could lead to lower short-term interest rates and an increase in demand for Federal Reserve RRPs later this year, which is also the time when many market participants expect the FOMC to begin policy firming.	61	6
201507	135	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Turning to other SOMA-related developments, the Desk is planning to initiate CUSIP aggregation of agency MBS beginning next month, as highlighted in the top-right panel.	61	6
201507	136	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Recall that in early 2011, the Desk performed a similar operation that resulted in cost savings to the SOMA portfolio and significant portfolio management benefits.	61	6
201507	137	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	We have similar goals now and believe this measure would also make it easier to sell SOMA’s MBS holdings, should the Committee direct the Desk to do so in the future.	61	6
201507	138	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk plans to aggregate roughly 60,000 individual Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac securities into approximately 350 new pools, representing a combined face value of $1.27 trillion.	61	6
201507	139	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	As described in a memo circulated prior to the meeting, the Desk intends to release a statement as well as FAQs this Friday and to start aggregation in mid-August.	61	6
201507	140	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Once we begin the aggregation process, we expect that the associated costs will be recovered through custodial cost savings within two to four years.	61	6
201507	141	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Should the Committee decide to commence policy firming at this meeting, we would plan to postpone the start of CUSIP aggregation to avoid complicating the communications associated with liftoff.	61	6
201507	142	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	As a final administrative update, I would like to make you aware that a summary of the daily planning call between Desk and Monetary Affairs staff is now being posted each day on the Class II FOMC–Restricted (FR) section of MarketSource.	61	6
201507	143	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk would be happy to assist you in receiving this information, if interested.	61	6
201507	144	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	That concludes our prepared remarks.	61	6
201507	145	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	We would be happy to take questions.	61	6

201507	198	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Our next agenda item has to do with normalization planning, and I’m going to call on Lorie to begin.	96	9
201507	199	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	200	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	I will be referring to “Material for Briefing on Normalization.”	96	9
201507	201	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Jim Clouse and I will summarize the state of preparations related to the approach the Committee has said it intends to take to normalize the stance of monetary policy.	96	9
201507	202	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Having conducted nearly two years of daily test operations, the Desk is prepared to implement an ON RRP facility to support IOER in moving the effective federal funds rate into the target range when the FOMC commences policy firming.	96	9
201507	203	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	At that time, the domestic policy directive that governs the Desk’s conduct of open market operations will need to incorporate instructions for the ON RRP facility and term RRPs.	96	9
201507	204	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The ON RRP test operations that have been conducted under the resolution passed by the Committee last December will then cease.	96	9
201507	205	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The draft policy implementation note associated with alternative C in this meeting’s Tealbook B presents a revised proposal for the Desk directive at the time of liftoff.	96	9
201507	206	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	This takes into account your feedback on the draft directive that Thomas presented at the June meeting.	96	9
201507	207	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	I would like to highlight three key elements of the draft directive, which are summarized in your first panel.	96	9
201507	208	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	First, we have added an effective date to the directive.	96	9
201507	209	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The staff recommends that changes in the FOMC’s target range for the federal funds rate as well as changes to all overnight administered rates—namely, the IOER and IORR rates, the ON RRP rate, and the primary credit rate—be effective the day following the announcement of the Committee’s policy decision.	96	9
201507	210	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	This marks a departure from the Federal Reserve’s past practice.	96	9
201507	211	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	However, it will allow changes in the full set of overnight administered rates to be introduced concurrently in support of an FOMC decision to change the target range, increasing the likelihood of the effective federal funds rate trading within the target range each day.	96	9
201507	212	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in your second panel, this new convention would be consistent with the practices of several other major central banks.	96	9
201507	213	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	It would also maximize the public’s understanding of the Committee’s policy framework.	96	9
201507	214	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	From an operating perspective, this approach is consistent with the staff’s recommendation that any intermeeting changes in administered rates be announced at 4:30 pm when most markets are closed and are therefore only able to take effect the next day.	96	9
201507	215	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Should the Committee support this approach, the staff recommends communicating the decision about the effective date for the other administered rates prior to liftoff, such as in the July minutes, as we have started to receive questions by the public on the expected timing of changes in the overnight administered rates when the Committee commences policy firming.	96	9
201507	216	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The second element of the draft directive to highlight is the clarification of the description of capacity for the ON RRP facility.	96	9
201507	217	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Your third panel illustrates the language in the draft directive that could apply if the cap was temporarily suspended, indicating that the Desk could conduct ON RRPs in amounts “limited only by the value of Treasury securities held outright in the SOMA that are available for such operations.”	96	9
201507	218	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	We believe this language is consistent with the spirit of a suspended cap while at the same time highlighting the practical limitations that preclude unlimited provision of ON RRPs.	96	9
201507	219	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk’s operating policy statement, which would be posted following the publication of the FOMC’s policy decision and implementation note, would explain how the staff would derive the operational limit and note that the value of Treasury securities in the SOMA available for RRP operations would be about $2 trillion.	96	9
201507	220	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Finally, as summarized in your fourth panel, the draft directive strikes the sentence in the current directive that states it “seeks conditions in reserve markets consistent with” the federal funds rate trading in the FOMC’s target  range, as the language would no longer be as reflective of policy implementation in the post-liftoff framework.	96	9
201507	221	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The draft, however, retains the directive’s broad instruction to the Desk to undertake open market operations “as necessary” to keep the federal funds rate in its target range.	96	9
201507	222	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	This language is followed by specific instructions to undertake overnight and term reverse repurchase agreements according to parameters approved by the Committee.	96	9
201507	223	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The baseline expectation is that reverse repos will be the only open market operations needed to support IOER to keep the effective federal funds rate in the FOMC’s target range.	96	9
201507	224	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Nonetheless, a directive that authorizes the Desk to conduct other types of open market operations, if necessary—such as repos if the effective federal funds rate was expected to print too high—could signal to the public that the Committee has given the Desk some latitude to respond quickly to unexpected circumstances.	96	9
201507	225	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Any use of such authority would be limited and aimed at addressing transitory factors, such as in response to a major payments system disruption.	96	9
201507	226	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	In the event of more persistent issues, the FOMC may choose to revise its guidance to the Desk.	96	9
201507	227	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk would consult with the Chair and inform the FOMC of any plans to conduct open market operations other than the reverse repos specified in the directive.	96	9
201507	228	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	In addition to the revisions I have highlighted, other changes as shown in the draft directive for alternative C in Tealbook B, are generally consistent with the housekeeping-type changes that Thomas presented to the Committee in June.	96	9
201507	229	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	To summarize, at the June meeting you unanimously supported a proposal for the Federal Reserve to issue an implementation note that would communicate separately from the Committee’s postmeeting policy statement the specific measures the Federal Reserve was employing to implement the FOMC’s decision.	96	9
201507	230	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	This note will include the policy directive to the Desk that you ultimately adopt.	96	9
201507	231	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	We highlighted a few key elements of the draft directive for consideration, and the staff recommends the Committee communicate about the intended effective date of changes in the target range and administered rates in the upcoming minutes.	96	9
201507	232	2015-07-29	meeting	LOGAN	Jim will now discuss other elements of the implementation note.	96	9
201507	233	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	Thanks, Lorie.	96	9
201507	234	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	As shown in the second exhibit, the implementation note will include information on the key administered rates that will support policy normalization.	96	9
201507	235	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	Assuming that the FOMC initiates policy firming by raising the target range from 0 to 25 basis points to 25 to 50 basis points, the ON RRP rate would be set at 25 basis points, and the interest rates on required and excess reserves would both be set at 50 basis points.	96	9
201507	236	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	In discussing changes in discount rates at the April FOMC meeting, participants generally seemed to favor maintaining the primary credit rate at the current spread of 50 basis points above the top of the target range for the federal funds rate for some time after liftoff.	96	9
201507	237	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	As noted in the last bulleted item in the implementation note, that would imply a primary credit rate of 100 basis points immediately after liftoff.	96	9
201507	238	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	As Lorie noted, the staff is recommending that all of these changes in administered rates take effect on the day following the FOMC announcement.	96	9
201507	239	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	As noted in previous discussions, changes in some of the administered rates require Board approval.	96	9
201507	240	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	Changes in the interest rates on reserves, required and excess, could be approved through a Board vote on the same day as the FOMC meeting.	96	9
201507	241	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	Approval for changes in the primary credit rate are somewhat more involved in light of the role of the Boards of Directors of Reserve Banks in the discount rate-setting process.	96	9
201507	242	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	On the day of any meeting in which the FOMC changes the target range for the federal funds rate, the Board could approve any existing requests by Reserve Banks for discount rate changes to the new rate to be effective on the next business day.	96	9
201507	243	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	In addition, any requests for discount rate changes from Reserve Banks received in the afternoon following the conclusion of the FOMC meeting or on the subsequent business day would be approved by the Board Secretary under delegated authority with the same effective date.	96	9
201507	244	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	These procedures are the same as those that have been in place for many years, except for the effective date.	96	9
201507	245	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	For completeness, it is worth noting that the rates for two other forms of discount window lending—secondary credit and seasonal credit—are set by formulas routinely proposed by the Reserve Banks and approved by the Board.	96	9
201507	246	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	The secondary credit rate is set at 50 basis points above the primary credit rate.	96	9
201507	247	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	The seasonal credit rate is established every two weeks based on the average effective federal funds rate and the 90-day CD rate over the previous reserve maintenance period.	96	9
201507	248	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	These rates are not included in the proposed implementation note because they have no significant implications for the process of policy normalization.	96	9
201507	249	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	If policymakers wished to employ term draining tools—the term deposit facility or term RRP—the implementation note could include the important details of those operations.	96	9
201507	250	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	Turning to two other items related to normalization, as discussed in memos prepared for the June FOMC meeting, the Desk will be expanding its coverage of money market developments in the morning calls in the period immediately after liftoff.	96	9
201507	251	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	Moreover, the staff will brief policymakers each day at 2 pm in the days immediately after liftoff to review market developments and the effectiveness of policy implementation.	96	9
201507	252	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	Those afternoon briefings can be readily converted to formal FOMC and Board meetings as necessary should policymakers wish to discuss and implement any changes in the approach to policy normalization.	96	9
201507	253	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	Finally, as discussed in previous FOMC meetings, the staff proposed a change to the methodology for the calculation of interest payments on reserves.	96	9
201507	254	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	After a public- comment period, the Board approved that change, and it became effective in the maintenance period that began last Thursday.	96	9
201507	255	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	The change in methodology should support the role of IOER as a policy normalization tool by ensuring that increases in the IOER rate are immediately reflected in higher interest payments to depository institutions.	96	9
201507	256	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	In particular, interest payments are now based primarily on the level of balances that a depository institution maintains each day and the level of the IOER rate in effect that day.	96	9
201507	257	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	That structure should help to ensure that an increase in the IOER rate immediately provides incentives for depository institutions to bid at higher rates in overnight funding markets and to require a rate of return at least as high as IOER on their investments in assets other than reserve balances.	96	9
201507	258	2015-07-29	meeting	CLOUSE	That concludes our prepared remarks.	96	9

201507	315	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Now we’re ready to move along to our next topic, which is reinvestment policy.	96	9
201507	316	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We’re going to call on Beth Klee to start us off.	96	9
201507	317	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	318	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Julie Remache and I will be referring to the handout labeled “Material for Briefing on SOMA Reinvestment Policy.”	96	9
201507	319	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	As you know, the Policy Normalization Principles and Plans state that the Committee expects to cease, or commence phasing out, reinvestments of principal on securities held in the SOMA after it begins increasing the target range for the federal funds rate, and that timing will depend on how economic and financial conditions and the economic outlook evolve.	96	9
201507	320	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	As background for the Committee’s discussion on reinvestments, the staff prepared the memo titled “Reinvestments Considerations.”	96	9
201507	321	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	The memo described several strategies that you could take and reviewed a range of issues associated with each strategy.	96	9
201507	322	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	We also suggested questions to help structure your discussion of this topic.	96	9
201507	323	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	The top two panels of your first exhibit summarize the strategies as well as some pros and cons of each.	96	9
201507	324	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	As shown in the top panel, the first set of strategies are calendar dependent—reinvestments would cease at a set date or after a specified interval following the initial firming of the federal funds rate.	96	9
201507	325	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	The Committee could follow a strictly calendar-dependent strategy or make the date conditional on macroeconomic conditions.	96	9
201507	326	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Of note, a conditional calendar-based strategy is similar to that employed in the forward guidance for the federal funds rate from 2011 to 2012.	96	9
201507	327	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	You may want to use a date for communicating the anticipated end of reinvestments if you are reasonably confident that a reversal of the decision to cease reinvestments will not be necessary or because you view it as a parsimonious and effective approach to communicate economic conditionality.	96	9
201507	328	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	As noted to the right, a calendar-based strategy would be relatively straightforward to communicate to the public.	96	9
201507	329	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	In addition, it would offer some certainty regarding the timing of the ceasing of reinvestments, and by implication, the path of the SOMA portfolio.	96	9
201507	330	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	These features could also be considered drawbacks in some circumstances, as this strategy could be seen as inflexible.	96	9
201507	331	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	In particular, the Committee could feel that, perhaps even with some conditionality, it could be difficult to deviate from the announced schedule even if the economy behaves much differently than expected.	96	9
201507	332	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Under those scenarios, the Federal Reserve’s action, or lack thereof, could send a confusing signal.	96	9
201507	333	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	As shown in the middle panel, the second set of strategies are state-dependent; reinvestments would cease based on specified economic conditions.	96	9
201507	334	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	The Committee could follow a quantitative state-dependent strategy wherein redemptions would commence based on a particular macroeconomic threshold.	96	9
201507	335	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	A quantitative state- dependent threshold strategy was used to provide forward guidance about the federal funds rate from 2012 to 2014.	96	9
201507	336	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Another variation of a state-dependent strategy would be one that offered qualitative guidance regarding the conditions under which the Committee expects to cease reinvestments—not unlike the current guidance for the federal funds rate.	96	9
201507	337	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	You may want to employ a state-dependent strategy if you believe doing so provides clear communications or if it enhances the “automatic stabilizer function” of monetary policy.	96	9
201507	338	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	That is, if the economy improves less rapidly than expected, the cessation of reinvestments would occur later; they would also cease sooner if the economy improves more rapidly.	96	9
201507	339	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Consequently, a state-dependent strategy might also reduce the possibility of returning to the effective lower bound.	96	9
201507	340	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Important challenges would be determining the appropriate threshold or trigger under a quantitative approach or being sufficiently clear about your reaction function under a qualitative approach.	96	9
201507	341	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	A state-dependent approach provides less certainty about the path of SOMA assets, but that consideration might be seen as offset by the improved economic responsiveness of this strategy.	96	9
201507	342	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	The details of either a calendar-dependent or state-dependent strategy would, of course, affect the path of the Federal Reserve’s balance sheet over time.	96	9
201507	343	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	To illustrate how the details matter, the bottom-left panel presents scenarios under the modal outlook in which reinvestments end fairly soon after liftoff or much later.	96	9
201507	344	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	The Tealbook baseline, the black line, is based on the assumption that reinvestments cease six months after initial policy firming, and that the federal funds rate will be around 60 basis points at that time.	96	9
201507	345	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	The dashed blue line illustrates a scenario where reinvestments cease nearly two years after liftoff, when the funds rate reaches 2 percent.	96	9
201507	346	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Even though reinvestments continue for 16 months longer than in the baseline, normalization of the size of the balance sheet is delayed only about 9 months, in part because large amounts of securities are expected to mature around the time of normalization of the size of the balance sheet.	96	9
201507	347	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	However, as shown in the bottom-right panel, the funds rate would be at a higher level when reinvestments end, incorporating some insurance against possible zero lower bound scenarios.	96	9
201507	348	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Still, the difference between the two funds rate paths is small, and this suggests that the benefit of extending reinvestments could potentially be modest.	96	9
201507	349	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	Of course, it is possible that there are effects of continuing or ceasing reinvestment beyond those captured in our models.	96	9
201507	350	2015-07-29	meeting	KLEE	To that end, Julie will now discuss market-specific considerations and expectations associated with ceasing reinvestments.	96	9
201507	351	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Thank you, Beth.	96	9
201507	352	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	In thinking about the strategy to end reinvestments, there are some market-specific issues which the Committee may wish to consider.	96	9
201507	353	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	In the Treasury market, the Federal Reserve’s redemption of maturing securities will require the Treasury to auction more securities to the public than if the SOMA continues to roll over its Treasury holdings.	96	9
201507	354	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	As shown in the top panel of exhibit 2, maturing securities from the SOMA—shown in blue—would add, on average, 40 percent to the projected increase in public holdings from 2016 through 2020 relative to the increase arising from the budget deficit—shown in red.	96	9
201507	355	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	While these total increases are large, they are less than those recorded during the recession that followed the financial crisis.	96	9
201507	356	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	That said, 2008 to 2009 was a period in which demand for Treasury securities was elevated, and it remains to be seen how the market would adjust without this boost to demand.	96	9
201507	357	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	While the market response to ending reinvestments will depend on the level and dispersion of market expectations for the path of the portfolio—which I will discuss in just a moment—in the case of Treasury securities, the effect will also be determined by the Treasury’s decisions about the maturity profile of the additional securities it issues.	96	9
201507	358	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	The Treasury might initially respond to the onset of SOMA redemptions by issuing more bills.	96	9
201507	359	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Over time, however, the Treasury would likely shift this financing toward longer-maturity coupon securities.	96	9
201507	360	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	In the MBS market, participants have expressed more concern about potential market strains.	96	9
201507	361	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	During the period where the Federal Reserve continues to reinvest the principal it receives from its MBS holdings, it will be purchasing approximately 30 percent of gross TBA-eligible issuance, a proportionately larger amount than in the Treasury market.	96	9
201507	362	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	In addition, the inherent difficulties in accurately predicting prepayment activity implies considerable uncertainty about the dollar amount of reinvestments, limiting the extent to which markets can fully anticipate the effect of a decision to cease reinvestments.	96	9
201507	363	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	The bottom panel of your exhibit shows net changes in the Federal Reserve’s MBS activity over time.	96	9
201507	364	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Focusing on the black line, it highlights that in March 2010, following the completion of the first round of asset purchases, the shift in Federal Reserve participation in the mortgage market was larger than what is projected based on the current forecast, shown by the dotted portion of the line in early 2016.	96	9
201507	365	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Overall, the market withstood that change without significant disruption.	96	9
201507	366	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	That said, the underlying structure of the market has shifted since then, with greater concentration among dealers and more constrained balance sheets due to the changing regulatory environment.	96	9
201507	367	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	These concerns may support a decision to phase out reinvestments over time rather than ceasing them all at once.	96	9
201507	368	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	On the one hand, while a well-telegraphed end to reinvestments is not likely to lead to significant disruptions, phasing out reinvestments may provide insurance against this possibility and, if executed over a few quarters, would likely not have significantly different macroeconomic effects compared with a case in which cessation occurred all at once.	96	9
201507	369	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	On the other hand, it would lead to a slower decline in the portfolio, though the change would only extend the timing of the normalization of the size of the portfolio by a few months.	96	9
201507	370	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	The Committee may also wish to consider phasing out reinvestments in order to address the uneven pattern of redemptions.	96	9
201507	371	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	As shown in the top panel of exhibit 3, the amount of maturing Treasury securities held by the SOMA—shown by the red bars—will vary between $2 billion and $39 billion per month in 2016.	96	9
201507	372	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Although the projection of MBS principal payments—shown by the blue bars—appears smooth and steady, actual prepayments will vary over time as a function of prepayment behavior.	96	9
201507	373	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Smoothing redemptions may, on the margin, help the market absorb the new supply without a noticeable effect on the overall trajectory of the balance sheet or the associated withdrawal of accommodation.	96	9
201507	374	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	An incidental benefit of phasing out Treasury reinvestments over time would be to add Treasury benchmark securities to the SOMA portfolio during the reinvestment period, which could then be made available to lend.	96	9
201507	375	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	The SOMA has not held benchmark securities for some time because of the sales under the System’s maturity extension program, but making securities available to lend from the SOMA is helpful when there is tightness in the specials repo market.	96	9
201507	376	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	If the Committee wished to phase reinvestments out over time, it could do so in a number of ways.	96	9
201507	377	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	A straightforward approach would be to reinvest a decreasing proportion of Treasury maturities or MBS principal payments over time.	96	9
201507	378	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	This would result in a slower reduction in the portfolio and would smooth the pattern of maturities and principal payments to some extent.	96	9
201507	379	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Another approach could involve setting a maximum dollar amount of securities that would be allowed to mature or prepay without reinvestment in each month and to increase the dollar amount over time.	96	9
201507	380	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	This would have a similar effect of slowing the reduction in the portfolio and would smooth the pattern of reductions more directly.	96	9
201507	381	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	As with the strategy to begin to cease reinvestments that Beth discussed, these strategies could be executed based on a set schedule, or they could be contingent on continued improvement in the economy.	96	9
201507	382	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Further staff work could be completed to evaluate these and other options should the Committee decide to phase out reinvestments.	96	9
201507	383	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Turning now to market expectations, as shown in the bottom-left panel of your exhibit, the median respondents to the Desk’s Survey of Primary Dealers and its Survey of Market Participants expected both Treasury security and MBS reinvestments to cease approximately seven months after liftoff, but there was a wide range around this figure, with some respondents expecting reinvestments to cease at liftoff and others expecting reinvestments to continue for more than a year.	96	9
201507	384	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	As shown in the bottom-right panel, respondents generally place the highest probability on reinvestments being gradually phased out over time.	96	9
201507	385	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	The median expectation is that, should reinvestments be phased out gradually, this would be done over a period of about 11 months for both Treasury securities and MBS, though again, expectations for this are dispersed.	96	9
201507	386	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Overall, respondents generally expect the reinvestment policies for Treasuries and MBS to be similar.	96	9
201507	387	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	While market participants are generally not focused on whether a decision about reinvestments would be specifically calendar or state dependent, many note that they expect the Committee to be attentive to economic and financial conditions and to take account of potential disruptions to market functioning and liquidity in determining the pace at which reinvestments could occur.	96	9
201507	388	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	In supporting this view, many cite the Committee’s Policy Normalization Principles and Plans statement and other communications emphasizing a gradual approach to normalization.	96	9
201507	389	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Some policymakers’ recent communications have reinforced these ideas, including the notion that a change in the reinvestment policy could be tied to the level of the federal funds target range.	96	9
201507	390	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	We should note that survey respondents and market participants indicate that they do not hold firm views about reinvestment, in light of the limited information available to them about the FOMC’s thinking on this topic.	96	9
201507	391	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	The final page of your handout provides the questions circulated to you previously.	96	9
201507	392	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	393	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	That concludes our prepared remarks.	96	9
201507	394	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	Beth and I would be happy to take questions.	96	9
201507	395	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201507	396	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Were there questions or comments?	96	9
201507	397	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	96	9
201507	398	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Yes, I just have a question about the phaseout.	96	9
201507	399	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Julie, you listed a whole bunch of arguments in favor of a phaseout.	96	9
201507	400	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In weighing these, would you describe them primarily in terms of market dislocations, disruptions, and other aspects of it, or is there really much of an economic argument in terms of macroeconomic goals here?	96	9
201507	401	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’m just hoping to clarify what is the advantage of a phaseout over, say, 6 to 12 months.	96	9
201507	402	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	I think the main advantage to considering a phaseout would be to address the potential risks related to market functioning.	96	9

201507	409	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	With the one caveat that in 2013, talking about what we might do in the future with a portfolio, in terms of the taper, had very big effects.	96	9
201507	410	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	And the model would say that it would have no effects.	96	9
201507	411	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	The model would say that it would have no effects.	96	9

201507	413	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	So it’s important to recognize, in terms of the market response, that it will depend on where market expectations are at the time and how dispersed they are.	96	9
201507	414	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	In thinking about the communications, that communication can clarify a range of expectations, and that could cause a change in market rates relative to before the announcement.	96	9
201507	415	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	96	9
201507	416	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	When you say “market rates,” and you talk about the taper, I guess the one market rate that seems most important is the mortgage rate.	96	9
201507	417	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	Can you imagine that mortgage rates would have some type of outsized effect?	96	9
201507	418	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	Is that what you’re talking about?	96	9
