201507	427	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Seeing none, why don’t we begin our go-round.	96	9
201507	428	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo is going to start us off.	96	9
201507	429	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you very much, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	430	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	I begin from the premise that the issue of when to cease reinvestments of the SOMA portfolio needs discussion among policymakers not only because of some of the considerations that Beth and Julie have just raised, but also because, while the funds rate and portfolio adjustments are both available monetary policy tools, we don’t regard them as perfect substitutes for one another.	96	9
201507	431	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Before answering the questions that were put to us in the staff memo, I want to start by specifying what I think are the salient differences between them, for our purposes.	96	9
201507	432	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	First, in our previous discussions of normalization policy, several participants have expressed the view that we should use only federal funds rate increases in the early stages of tightening so as to return as quickly as we can to a point where material federal funds rate reductions would be available as a response to a downturn in the economy.	96	9
201507	433	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The preference for federal funds rate reductions over additional SOMA purchases presumably arises from some combination of our sense of the relative efficacy of the two instruments in the contemplated deteriorating conditions and of concerns about institutional or external reactions to another LSAP program.	96	9
201507	434	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	This view seems quite sensible, though I might note in passing that the caution inherent in this view would also seem to argue, at least at the margin, for a delay in a start to tightening in order to reduce the chances of a downturn that would require a policy reversal.	96	9
201507	435	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	A second difference is the possibility that through some combination of direct and signaling effects, cessation of reinvestments in Treasury securities would more directly affect the longer end of the yield curve.	96	9
201507	436	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Right now, the average duration of Treasury securities in our portfolio is around seven years.	96	9
201507	437	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Reinvestments would probably have a duration of five to six years.	96	9
201507	438	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	So stopping reinvestments would increase the supply of longer-duration bonds in the market.	96	9
201507	439	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	This possibility would become significant if, as some observers have speculated, our initial increases in the federal funds rate do not yield proportionate increases further out on the curve, an outcome presumably of some importance if the Committee’s efforts to tighten financial conditions are to be effective in the real economy.	96	9
201507	440	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Of course, if the shape of the curve were determined overwhelmingly by market expectations of future short-term rates plus a term premium, then theoretically an anticipated reduction in our balance sheet size shouldn’t affect longer-term yields.	96	9
201507	441	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	But I think we’ve seen in recent years that actual changes in the supply of securities can have some effects that are not altogether driven by rational expectations of future conditions.	96	9
201507	442	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Third, if the ON RRP program becomes and remains larger because of the quantity of reserves associated with our large balance sheet, then the concerns I’ve previously expressed with respect to financial stability might be mitigated through earlier measures to reduce its size.	96	9
201507	443	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Of course, the size of the ON RRP after liftoff will depend on many factors, including the Treasury’s decisions on bill issuance and the speed with which banks begin to raise the rates they pay on deposits.	96	9
201507	444	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	And depending on when we began roll-offs, the mitigating effect might be pretty modest and more about signaling than direct effects.	96	9
201507	445	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	But the possibility raised in the recent memo to Reserve Bank research directors—that the demand for ON RRP might increase over time, rather than stabilize or decline—is another reminder of why we should keep the financial-stability and market-structure issues in mind.	96	9
201507	446	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Fourth, and finally, the fact that we hold a lot of MBS means that portfolio adjustment might have a disproportionate effect on mortgage markets relative to federal funds rate increases.	96	9
201507	447	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Our decisions on reinvestment policy will be usefully informed by considering which of these differences are very likely to be important for our policies and which would be important only if less probable contingencies were to arise.	96	9
201507	448	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The fact that we don’t know at the outset of normalization whether we will need to react to a near- or medium-term downturn argues for pursuing initial tightening solely through federal funds rate increases so as to reacquire as quickly as possible the less controversial—and arguably more effective—tool of funds rate decreases.	96	9
201507	449	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	But I wouldn’t want to adopt a policy that ruled out an earlier cessation of rollovers in the event that developments affecting the yield curve or the ON RRP program made such a step advisable.	96	9
201507	450	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	In short, my current thinking is that our presumption should be that we will raise rates several times before ending reinvestments, but that we might move more quickly if we observe post-liftoff difficulties in these other areas.	96	9
201507	451	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Looking at things this way, I’d be disinclined to get very specific in an ex-ante communication strategy.	96	9
201507	452	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Calendar guidance, even conditional, would almost surely be read as a near commitment.	96	9
201507	453	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	And I don’t see how to sensibly use economic indicators such as unemployment or inflation as triggers because those kinds of indicators are relevant to the overall pace of tightening through both instruments.	96	9
201507	454	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The reasons for maintaining some optionality concerning portfolio practices pertain to financial conditions, which would be particularly difficult to capture in quantitative terms, especially because there are some quite distinct considerations.	96	9
201507	455	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	I think this argues for only a modest change in the policy we announced in our normalization principles last fall—namely, that the timing of the cessation of reinvestment will depend on how economic and financial conditions and the economic outlook evolve.	96	9
201507	456	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The modest change would be to add something to reflect that aim of reacquiring interest rate reductions as a policy tool.	96	9
201507	457	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	One possible formulation—although I’m sure there are others that would capture the thought, and I think Vice Chairman Dudley has got one—would be to echo the Bank of England, which in various communications has indicated that the Monetary Policy Committee is not likely to change the size of the Bank’s balance sheet until the Bank rate has reached a level from which it could be cut materially if needed.	96	9
201507	458	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	It’s worth noting that the Bank of England has kept this position pretty general and has not incorporated it into formal statements of monetary policy.	96	9
201507	459	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	It’s been mentioned in some FAQs, referred to in its quarterly Inflation Reports, and, in even more general terms, mentioned by Governor Carney in testimony to a parliamentary committee.	96	9
201507	460	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	It seems to me very sensible for us to emulate the Bank of England and not make too big a deal of all this so as to avoid creating specific expectations that might be taken as near commitments or used as benchmarks to evaluate how normalization is going.	96	9
201507	461	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	That suggests to me that we should communicate this modest elaboration of our intentions through the minutes or through an answer by the Chair to a question at a press conference.	96	9
201507	462	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Next, I’d note that the bunching of maturing Treasuries in our portfolio would happily coincide with the approach I’ve just suggested, assuming our first funds rate increase happens later this year.	96	9
201507	463	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Right now, relatively small amounts are maturing each month.	96	9
201507	464	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	But in the period from February to May 2016, as one of the charts that they distributed shows, we have a substantial jump in maturing Treasuries to $128 billion over those four months.	96	9
201507	465	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Then there’s a pattern of a few low months followed by one higher month until early 2018, when the amounts for both higher- and lower-maturity months increase substantially.	96	9
201507	466	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	If we thought in terms of ceasing reinvestments in the second half of next year, we would have given ourselves time to make a few federal funds rate increases, assuming the central tendency of the Committee holds, and yet still have a period of relatively low amounts maturing monthly so as not to tighten financial conditions very much via portfolio runoff, at least for a while.	96	9
201507	467	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Finally, with respect to the issue of full cessation or phaseout of reinvestments, I feel differently about Treasury securities and MBS.	96	9
201507	468	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	For Treasury securities, I’d probably favor ceasing most reinvestments immediately or soon after we make the decision to move ahead, particularly if that is in a period when relatively small amounts were maturing.	96	9
201507	469	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	However, in light of the fact that the pattern of maturation is quite uneven, I’d be interested in Simon Potter’s views as to whether it would be a good idea to smooth out the reduction in our Treasury portfolio as well as whether there are other reasons to continue to roll over a modest amount for some period of time, which I think Julie Remache alluded to.	96	9
201507	470	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	As to MBS, because our portfolio accounts for a substantially greater share of that market, it’s probably better to phase out reinvestment of agency MBS, though as to precisely how, I would again want to be guided by advice from the Desk.	96	9
201507	471	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	472	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201507	473	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	96	9
201507	474	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you.	96	9
201507	475	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	As posed in the staff memo, there are two essential issues.	96	9
201507	476	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	First, should the process of ending reinvestments be based on calendar time or just state dependent?	96	9
201507	477	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, when we end the process of reinvestment, should we do this by tapering or instead by “cold turkey,” and should the process be the same for Treasury securities and agency MBS?	96	9
201507	478	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Turning to the first point, I come out pretty close to what Governor Tarullo said.	96	9
201507	479	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m on the side of qualitative state-dependent guidance.	96	9
201507	480	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	State-dependent guidance has a number of advantages over calendar-based guidance.	96	9
201507	481	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	First, working through the expectations channel, state dependency would automatically add or subtract support to the economy as incoming data pushes back or pulls in expectations about the end of the timing of reinvestments.	96	9
201507	482	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, this is not a particularly strong effect in most states of the world, but it might be very helpful if the draw on the outlook was particularly negative.	96	9
201507	483	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, it seems prudent to avoid prematurely committing to end reinvestments, in view of the asymmetry of the policy options should the economy prove weaker than expected.	96	9
201507	484	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If the economy were weaker than expected, our tools to provide support are limited in that direction.	96	9
201507	485	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Reversing course and stopping the balance sheet from shrinking once the process has begun—we have that option—would be difficult to do in practice, and the scope for policy accommodation by reducing short-term interest rates would be quite limited for some time by the proximity of the zero lower bound.	96	9
201507	486	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I prefer qualitative state-dependent guidance rather than defining particular variables as triggers for action.	96	9
201507	487	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	This is motivated by my view that the end of reinvestments should be driven by the likelihood that we’ll be forced to return to the effective lower bound sometime in the relatively near future, and that likelihood simply cannot be summed up by a single parameter.	96	9
201507	488	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	For example, I could imagine ending reinvestments at a relatively low federal funds rate if the economy had considerable forward momentum or waiting a bit longer if the momentum were less strong or if there were greater risks that it might not be sustained in the future.	96	9
201507	489	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The qualitative standard that I have in mind would read something like this, which I think tracks the Bank of England approach:  “reasonable confidence that the economic outlook will not warrant a return to the zero lower bound in the next few years”—or something similar.	96	9
201507	490	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In my mind, this probably would not imply ending reinvestments until the federal funds rate was at least 1 percent, but probably even higher, depending on the economy’s forward momentum and the risks to the outlook that were in place at that time.	96	9
201507	491	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, the major downside to qualitative state-dependent guidance is it makes it a much bigger deal when we finally actually do decide to shrink the balance sheet.	96	9
201507	492	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Thus, there is a greater risk, in this approach, of a bigger market reaction.	96	9
201507	493	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	However, I think this risk can be lessened by good communications.	96	9
201507	494	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	As long as we’re clear about what’s driving our thinking, then market participants should be able to think along with us and anticipate our decision.	96	9
201507	495	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	We could also reduce the risk of surprise by communicating our thinking in the FOMC minutes or in the Chair’s press conference.	96	9
201507	496	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	My point is that the risk of surprising and destabilizing the markets is under our control to a large extent, so that we can minimize the risk of an outsized market reaction.	96	9
201507	497	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, for calendar-based guidance, it strikes me that the major benefit is that it damps any effect from the decision to begin to end the reinvestment process.	96	9
201507	498	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	There’s no signal from the decision in terms of timing—it’s already been folded in mechanically with the liftoff decision.	96	9
201507	499	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	This means that when redemption and wind-down begin, not much should happen because there’s not a strong signal of any change in view on the part of the Federal Reserve.	96	9
201507	500	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But this is offset by two significant negatives.	96	9
201507	501	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	First, as the start of ending the reinvestment process will represent a tightening of policy, it contradicts what we’ve been saying—namely, that monetary policy decisions are data dependent.	96	9
201507	502	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If the timing of liftoff, which is a move to less accommodation, is data dependent, logic would imply that other means of tightening policy should also be data dependent.	96	9
201507	503	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, it seems to me that we want to be careful about ending reinvestments prematurely.	96	9
201507	504	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	That is because once we begin on that path, it may be hard to reverse course—that is, to start reinvesting, and even harder to expand the balance sheet again.	96	9
201507	505	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I, for one, want to be highly confident that we are unlikely to have to return to the zero lower bound in the near future before ending reinvestments.	96	9
201507	506	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m not sure how to reconcile that with calendar- based guidance unless I push the calendar-based guidance very far off into the future, an option that I don’t think is reasonably on the table.	96	9
201507	507	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Turning next to the issue of how to end reinvestments, I would favor tapering, and I would not distinguish between Treasury securities and agency MBS.	96	9
201507	508	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I favor tapering because it reduces the risk of any damage to market function.	96	9
201507	509	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	We just don’t know what those risks are, and I don’t see why you’d want to take a chance when you are not really sure how big those risks are.	96	9
201507	510	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Doing it this way also would be generally consistent with current market expectations.	96	9
201507	511	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The cost in terms of delaying the normalization of the balance sheet are low as long as the taper is not stretched over a long period—that is, as long as it’s not stretched out for more than a year or so.	96	9
201507	512	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I wouldn’t distinguish between Treasury securities and agency MBS because I’m not convinced that we really have a strong compelling reason to do so.	96	9
201507	513	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If you weren’t tapering, you might want to differentiate, because the risk to market functioning might differ.	96	9
201507	514	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But because tapering addresses that market-functioning risk directly, then there no longer seems to be a case for differentiation once you’ve made the decision to taper.	96	9
201507	515	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, assuming that tapering is the way the Committee ultimately wants to go, the next question would be the length and the form of taper.	96	9
201507	516	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I assume you don’t need to stretch out the taper very long, but I’d be interested in hearing from the staff about the pros and cons of a shorter versus longer taper.	96	9
201507	517	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the form of the taper, as Julie said, there are a number of ways to go.	96	9
201507	518	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	You can reduce the amount of reinvestment by a fixed percentage each month, or you can reduce it by a fixed dollar amount.	96	9
201507	519	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	These have different characteristics in terms of the risk to market function and the trajectory of the balance sheet.	96	9
201507	520	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m not sure which of these has better properties, frankly, so I would encourage the staff to come back with some proposals.	96	9
201507	521	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If we decide that tapering is the way to go, what is the best way to do it and why, because it’s not obvious?	96	9
201507	522	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Do you want to have more predictability on the amount of reinvestment being reduced each month, or do you want to have more predictability in terms of the path of the balance sheet each month?	96	9
201507	523	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s not obvious to me which is right.	96	9
201507	524	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I think it’s really important that we do clarify what we think about reinvestments, because when we lift off, the Chair is going to go to the press conference and one of the first questions is going to be, “Okay, now that you have lifted off, what are you going to do about reinvestments?”	96	9
201507	525	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I think the more we can clarify that matter before we get to that point, I think that would be a good place for the Committee to be.	96	9
201507	526	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you.	96	9
201507	527	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Agreed.	96	9
201507	528	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201507	529	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	96	9
201507	530	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	531	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, this especially is timely.	96	9
201507	532	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’m increasingly being asked about our balance sheet normalization plans, and prudent planning and good communication argue for settling on a strategy and tactics in advance of liftoff.	96	9
201507	533	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Like Governor Tarullo, I kind of stepped back when I got the memo and the questions.	96	9
201507	534	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I recall something that President Evans said when I first became president.	96	9
201507	535	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	When I answered the questions in the memo, he said, “That’s a rookie mistake.”	96	9
201507	536	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	[Laughter]	96	9
201507	537	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’ve been in the job now roughly four and a quarter years, so I’m not making the same rookie mistakes anymore.	96	9
201507	538	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Like Government Tarullo, I looked back and said, “What are we trying to accomplish here?	96	9
201507	539	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Under what conditions would certain approaches work better than others?”	96	9
201507	540	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	And that led me to think again about the issue of what the strategy is, and from that perspective consider the tactics or some of the questions more in the context of thinking about it in terms of what’s our strategy with regard to this.	96	9
201507	541	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	One possible strategy would treat the balance sheet—and I actually was struck by the fact that the memo was kind of pushing this way—as an active policy tool on par with the funds rate.	96	9
201507	542	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’re looking at economic conditions, looking at the forecast, deciding whether it’s time to end reinvestment or to pare back on reinvestment.	96	9
201507	543	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I didn’t think anyone would use the word “taper” again—I’m surprised by that.	96	9
201507	544	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	But really, you’re thinking the balance sheet would be adjusted based on economic conditions, and our policy communications would highlight the intentions about both the balance sheet and the funds rate.	96	9
201507	545	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	The other strategy is to put management of the balance sheet into the background, and instead focus policy actions and communications squarely on the funds rate.	96	9
201507	546	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In this case, the balance sheet reductions are aligned with the overall thrust of policy, obviously driven by our macroeconomic goals.	96	9
201507	547	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	But they wouldn’t be actively managed in the same way as the policy lever.	96	9
201507	548	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	So I strongly prefer the latter strategy.	96	9
201507	549	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	The Committee and financial market participants have a much better understanding of and more confidence in using the federal funds rate to conduct and communicate monetary policy.	96	9
201507	550	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In the past—notably during the taper tantrum—markets have viewed our balance sheet communications as signals about our intentions regarding the future path of the funds rate.	96	9
201507	551	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	A clear subordination of the balance sheet management to the funds rate would help avoid such confusion in the future.	96	9
201507	552	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In addition, the primacy of the funds rate is consistent with our treatment of other supporting tools in our normalization plans, such as the IOER and the overnight reverse repo facilities.	96	9
201507	553	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	And, finally, keeping the balance sheet actions in the background would be consistent with our earlier statement on policy normalization—that is, it indicated that reductions in the size of the balance sheet would be gradual and predictable.	96	9
201507	554	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In the context of these strategic considerations, I think our recent experience with funds rate forward guidance and with expanding the balance sheet through QE provides a couple of important lessons for the future.	96	9
201507	555	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	To begin with, date-based forward-looking policy statements boxed us in at times in arbitrary ways.	96	9
201507	556	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Similarly, setting policy thresholds based on economic variables proved problematic.	96	9
201507	557	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thus, I would prefer not to use any date-based guidance—I’m thinking about “six months” or some phrase like that—or economic variable thresholds for communicating the conditions to start reducing the balance sheet.	96	9
201507	558	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	With regard to using a specific level of the funds rate—say, 1 percent—as a threshold, I do see merits in that approach.	96	9
201507	559	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Specifically, it’s linking our policy decisions and our tools together.	96	9
201507	560	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	But I do think it could place undue attention and public speculation on what should be a relatively under-the-radar balance sheet action.	96	9
201507	561	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	What I would prefer is something qualitative.	96	9
201507	562	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	There have been a couple of suggestions about this, but I personally prefer the Chair’s eloquent public comments—namely, that we would begin the process of ceasing reinvestment after the Committee was comfortable that the normalization process was successfully under way.	96	9
201507	563	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I actually think that covers the comments that we’ve already heard about having the interest rate high enough that we’re in a comfortable place, taking into account the zero lower bound.	96	9
201507	564	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Actually, let me respond to the Vice Chairman’s comment.	96	9
201507	565	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do think that this reasonable confidence that we won’t return to the zero lower bound just opens a whole box of issues about what does that mean and how do we measure it.	96	9
201507	566	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	This reasonable confidence is something that’s hard to define, as we’ve learned.	96	9
201507	567	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	We should also keep in mind that the projected timeline for normalizing the balance sheet, absent asset sales, is already quite long.	96	9
201507	568	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	The baseline Board staff projection says that our balance sheet will still be putting downward pressure on term premiums for another 10 years.	96	9
201507	569	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In order to normalize the balance sheet before our retirements—all of our retirements—without resorting to asset sales, we shouldn’t wait too long to halt reinvestments.	96	9
201507	570	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’d also prefer to end reinvestments without any kind of taper or phaseout period.	96	9
201507	571	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’m still struggling with the argument for the phaseout.	96	9
201507	572	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Obviously, if it’s a phaseout over six months or something, I wouldn’t be opposed to that, but I still don’t quite see the strong argument for this.	96	9
201507	573	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Every time we’ve ended one of our QE programs or we’ve done the taper, we haven’t actually seen these market disruptions and dislocations that we’ve been so worried about.	96	9
201507	574	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I understood being worried about them the first few times, but I’m not sure why we’re still quite so worried about it.	96	9
201507	575	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	But, Julie, you said things have changed.	96	9
201507	576	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	So, again, maybe that’s prudent insurance against the possibility that this could be more of a problem.	96	9
201507	577	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do think it gets us back into the game of, if we do 50 percent of reinvestments the first time, or whatever we’re thinking about, it’s going to lead to the question, “Under what conditions are you going to do the next step-down or step-up?,” or however you want to phrase that.	96	9
201507	578	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	And so if we do a phaseout, I would argue that it should be somewhat mechanical, like we did the taper—obviously, with language describing it, depending on economic conditions, but really be more on autopilot.	96	9
201507	579	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I would argue that markets do seem to be sufficiently deep, that the flow considerations—again, a major concern associated with this—just don’t seem to be that important.	96	9
201507	580	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	And I would handle MBS and Treasury securities in the same way in terms of ending the reinvestments.	96	9
201507	581	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you very much.	96	9
201507	582	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201507	583	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	May I ask a clarifying question?	96	9
201507	584	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	You said that downward pressure of the balance sheet on term premiums would last 10 years?	96	9
201507	585	2015-07-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Yes.	96	9
201507	586	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	The size of the portfolio would be normalized in 2021, but because of the composition of the portfolio, it would still have a lot of MBS and some longer-duration securities.	96	9
201507	587	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So it would be a longer duration portfolio.	96	9
201507	588	2015-07-29	meeting	REMACHE	It would be another several years before the composition of the portfolio is also normalized.	96	9
201507	589	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I see.	96	9

201507	594	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	Could I just ask a question about the presentation?	96	9

201507	596	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	That made me go look at a part of Tealbook B I don’t look at very often.	96	9
201507	597	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	But I tried to dig up what the SOMA balance sheet holdings would actually look like, and the chart there is consistent with these peaks in maturities, right?	96	9

201507	603	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	96	9
201507	604	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	605	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In thinking about the normalization of the balance sheet, I have several principles that I would follow.	96	9
201507	606	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	First, balance sheet normalization should be implemented in a way that minimizes the likelihood of returning short- term rates to the zero lower bound.	96	9
201507	607	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	These are things highlighted by both Governor Tarullo and Vice Chairman Dudley.	96	9
201507	608	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Second, balance sheet normalization should be conducted to reduce the likelihood of taper tantrum-type disruptions by avoiding large, discrete changes.	96	9
201507	609	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Our models didn’t anticipate the taper tantrum, and I don’t think our models will anticipate any effect now.	96	9
201507	610	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	But I don’t have a lot of confidence in our ability to predict things that haven’t happened in the historical data.	96	9
201507	611	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In that historical period, we hadn’t been at the zero lower bound and we hadn’t had a large balance sheet.	96	9
201507	612	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	So I don’t think we should have too much certainty about what the effect might be.	96	9
201507	613	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Third, we should select and communicate a consistent, understandable redemption path, not necessarily tied to the somewhat arbitrary schedule of roll-offs and prepayments, but sized and timed to allow a smooth reduction in the size of the balance sheet.	96	9
201507	614	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Fourth, the plan should be to reduce the balance sheet at a fairly steady and predictable pace, but a pace that produces monetary tightening consistent with our macroeconomic forecasts.	96	9
201507	615	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Then we could use the federal funds target as the primary tool to respond to economic surprises that affect the forecast.	96	9
201507	616	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The federal funds rate channel is better understood than the balance sheet channel and the federal funds rate seems the more appropriate tool for making modest changes to the normalization process resulting from surprises in the incoming data.	96	9
201507	617	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	This is very similar to President Williams’s point on this.	96	9
201507	618	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Fifth, shrinking the balance sheet is tightening.	96	9
201507	619	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	We generally move the federal funds rate in 25 basis point increments.	96	9
201507	620	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would prefer the cumulative effect of redemptions over a one-year period to be sized to approximate a 25 basis point change in the federal funds rate.	96	9
201507	621	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In general, I envision a combination of funds rate policy and balance sheet reductions that follows the path outlined in the most recent Tealbooks, although with a somewhat more gradual start to the redemption program.	96	9
201507	622	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	That is, we would choose a liftoff date, raise the federal funds rate a couple of times, and, if things go according to plan, begin a tapered reduction in reinvestments after those initial increases.	96	9
201507	623	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	But it’s important to retain the sense of data dependence and flexibility as we anticipate this next phase of our normalization.	96	9
201507	624	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The logic of sequencing our exit so that liftoff precedes redemptions is to ensure the balance sheet actions would not delay liftoff from the zero lower bound.	96	9
201507	625	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Using that same logic, I suggest raising the federal funds rate target twice before beginning redemption tapering to ensure that we are well off the zero lower bound and that we have dealt with any complications in keeping the funds rate within our target range.	96	9
201507	626	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, the delay would provide time to assess the degree to which the increases in the federal funds rate are being transmitted to longer-term interest rates and whether our first set of actions has unexpectedly slowed the economy.	96	9
201507	627	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would then select and announce a path for redemptions that would reduce the chance of the announcement of balance sheet normalization creating a taper tantrum.	96	9
201507	628	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I consider the announcement of the tapering process as the third action in our tightening sequence.	96	9
201507	629	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	After we set the conditional path for redemptions, the criteria for additional tightening of the federal funds rate would be the same criteria I would use for beginning the balance sheet normalization process.	96	9
201507	630	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would not tie the announcement to calendar dates.	96	9
201507	631	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because earlier estimates of the effect of our balance sheet suggest that $500 billion of purchases was roughly equivalent to a 75 basis point decrease in the federal funds rate, a constant redemption flow of $15 billion a month for a year would translate to roughly a 25 basis point federal funds tightening over the course of a year.	96	9
201507	632	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	When a third tightening appears appropriate, I would announce the beginning of tapering of our balance sheet of $15 billion a month in redemptions.	96	9
201507	633	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If additional tightening of financial conditions was required, we could raise the federal funds rate at the same time as beginning the tapering process.	96	9
201507	634	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If the forecast unfolded as in the Tealbook, a gradual approach to tightening would be appropriate and the tapering process would be an alternative to raising the federal funds rate at that meeting.	96	9
201507	635	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of the composition of the redemptions, I would start with $5 billion of MBS redemptions and $10 billion in Treasury redemptions.	96	9
201507	636	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	This would minimize the chance that the announcement would cause a spike in mortgage rates.	96	9
201507	637	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If the housing market was becoming too ebullient, we could increase the proportion of MBS redemptions with or without subsequent increases in the flow of total redemptions.	96	9
201507	638	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	There is a financial-stability element in determining the size and composition of our redemptions.	96	9
201507	639	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Do we want to slow the housing sector or steepen the yield curve?	96	9
201507	640	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should increase the redemption size or increase the MBS share of redemptions.	96	9
201507	641	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In fact, the financial- stability tabletop conducted by the COP Financial Stability Committee included a scenario in which two of the presidents involved felt that the redemption or selling of longer-term assets might be one of the potential reactions to an overheating in the real estate market.	96	9
201507	642	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	For this reason, I would maintain some longer-term Treasury securities and MBS in our portfolio to preserve the option of a yield-curve tightening strategy should financial conditions in the future make that a desirable response to financial-stability concerns.	96	9
201507	643	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because our securities redemptions initially would be less than the balance sheet rollover, we also should discuss how the excess rollover funds should be reinvested.	96	9
201507	644	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If duration is one of the important factors in the effectiveness of the balance sheet as a monetary policy tool, reinvestment should be done to keep the proportion of MBS and the duration of the SOMA account unchanged other than for securities being redeemed.	96	9
201507	645	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, reinvesting in Treasury bills would tend to offset some of the tightening effects we are trying to accomplish through raising short-term rates.	96	9
201507	646	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	These concerns imply that the reinvesting should be concentrated in somewhat longer duration securities, which would pose complications down the road as it may alter the timing of roll-offs.	96	9
201507	647	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, this is something we could perhaps delegate to the Desk.	96	9
201507	648	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	649	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9

201507	652	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There seems to be an implicit notion that reducing the balance sheet will increase the probability of our hitting the zero lower bound.	96	9

201507	654	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Is it because—maybe I should go with what the Vice Chairman said—we think it would be very costly for us to ever increase the balance sheet again?	96	9

201507	663	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s fine, but even that doesn’t quite get you there, because if you were willing to reverse course and get yourself back up to the amount of the balance sheet we have in place now, whenever you’re faced with a shock, then you’re in the same place, essentially.	96	9

201507	684	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	685	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Much of the staff memo on reinvestment combines discussion of our reinvestment strategy with discussion of how we communicate about our strategy, especially what forward guidance we might provide.	96	9
201507	686	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	In fact, I think it’s fair to say the memo is virtually all about the forward guidance regarding our reinvestment strategy, rather than the strategy itself.	96	9
201507	687	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	And I found this a little bit surprising, because just earlier this year we ended the practice of providing forward guidance on our interest rate policy and went instead to a meeting-by-meeting basis for setting policy.	96	9
201507	688	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	And in our normalization plan document last September, we promised to give advance notice about asset sales, but we didn’t give any similar promise about reinvestment strategy.	96	9
201507	689	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	So, like President Williams, I found it useful to think first about what strategy we want to follow about our balance sheet and then to think about how we want to communicate about it.	96	9
201507	690	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Now, something stood out to me in the memo.	96	9
201507	691	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	The memo provides two scenarios regarding macroeconomic variables—one under an assumption of an early end to reinvestment and the other under an assumption of a later end to reinvestment.	96	9
201507	692	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	The early scenario is taken from the June Tealbook, and so that involves a particular interest rate path, presumably chosen appropriately—or the staff’s view of what’s appropriate, I’m not going to quibble with that.	96	9
201507	693	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	In the late scenario, the interest rate policy follows an inertial Taylor rule.	96	9
201507	694	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Now, because a later end to reinvestment by itself entails more accommodative policy, the funds rate is somewhat steeper in the later reinvestment path.	96	9
201507	695	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	But it only partially offsets the effect of a later end to reinvestment.	96	9
201507	696	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	The unemployment path is, accordingly, lower, and inflation, marginally higher.	96	9
201507	697	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Now, the staff points out that a funds rate path could be chosen that in the model would completely insulate our goal variables from the balance sheet effects of our reinvestment strategy.	96	9
201507	698	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	I’ve argued in the past that these balance sheet effects could be quite small, but let’s set that aside and just take these effects as given.	96	9
201507	699	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	I think it makes more sense to compare scenarios in which we are under the sort of complete-offset assumption.	96	9
201507	700	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	In other words, under the baseline, we’re assuming we’re setting interest rate policy appropriately.	96	9
201507	701	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	If we’re looking at a different timing for reinvestment, I think the sensible thing is to assume that if we adopted that, we would also set interest rate policy appropriately, and essentially that means projections regarding our goal variables would be invariant under the two scenarios.	96	9
201507	702	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	So the main effect of the choice of reinvestment is on the path of our balance sheet.	96	9
201507	703	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	We can sort of set aside unemployment and inflation.	96	9
201507	704	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Now, framed this way, that seems to a first approximation—of course, there are second-order issues, too—the useful way to think about it.	96	9
201507	705	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	To me, the choice seems pretty easy.	96	9
201507	706	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	I think an array of political economy considerations make it attractive for us to normalize the size of our balance sheet as soon as possible—sooner rather than later.	96	9
201507	707	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	I think we’d prefer as small a financial-system footprint as possible while maintaining the ability to accomplish our objectives and live up to our promise not to sell assets.	96	9
201507	708	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	I conclude that we should end reinvestment all at once, and soon.	96	9
201507	709	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Ideally, a meeting or two after we start raising rates seems reasonable.	96	9
201507	710	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Under that strategy, the interval between liftoff and ending reinvestment is relatively short, so forward guidance isn’t really that important a question.	96	9
201507	711	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Now, it strikes me that we could easily make this decision about reinvestment on a meeting-by-meeting basis and, at the appropriate time, simply announce that we’ve decided to stop reinvestment effective immediately in the same way we announced the beginnings of our quantitative easing programs and the beginning of tapering and the like.	96	9
201507	712	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	That would be consistent with our decision earlier this year to back away from forward guidance on interest rate policy, to go instead to a meeting-by-meeting basis.	96	9
201507	713	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	And I don’t see why we need forward guidance on ending reinvestment.	96	9
201507	714	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Let me just comment on the discussion about phaseout and market functioning.	96	9
201507	715	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	I have a history of questioning the staff on what they mean by market disruption.	96	9
201507	716	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	I think if we’re going to take some step like slowing down the end of reinvestments or delaying on the basis of the staff’s conjectures about market disruption, the Committee really ought to have a pretty concrete handle on what in the world that means.	96	9
201507	717	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	If prices move, if they get volatile on a couple of days, if something like that happens, I’m not sure why we should care, and I’m not sure what that should mean to us.	96	9
201507	718	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	If there’s something more fundamental, like some computers breaking down, I’d want to know about that—maybe that’s worth taking onboard.	96	9
201507	719	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	But I think we need a more concrete account of what “market disruption” means before we actually act on it.	96	9
201507	720	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9

201507	728	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	It would just be more complex to run that scenario.	96	9

201507	740	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Yes.	96	9
201507	741	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Just to follow up on that.	96	9
201507	742	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If we were to stop the reinvestments very quickly, we might still be very close to the zero lower bound.	96	9
201507	743	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	So the ability to offset seems a little bit inconsistent with starting the timing almost immediately.	96	9
201507	744	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	You’d be right if there’s enough room, but if there’s not much room, the ability to offset using the federal funds rate seems quite limited, so I think you’d have to pick one of those two.	96	9
201507	745	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If you really want an offset, you need enough room to be very confident you’re not going to hit the zero lower bound again.	96	9
201507	746	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	This is worth thinking about.	96	9
201507	747	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	In the macroeconomic literature, the standard treatment is that policy is sort of lexicographic, in that you only have the assets you need when interest rates are above zero.	96	9
201507	748	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	When you get to zero, then the balance sheet is what you use.	96	9
201507	749	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	And the presumption in a lot of models and a lot of discussions is last in, first out.	96	9
201507	750	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	On the way up, you’re running off the balance sheet and then raising rates.	96	9
201507	751	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	But we’re doing something different—for various reasons, we’re doing something different.	96	9
201507	752	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	We’re raising rates before we’re running off the balance sheet, and so we’re getting away from that lexicographic corner solution.	96	9
201507	753	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	And I think we need to be clear on why that is and what’s constraining us.	96	9
201507	754	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	If interest rates get to 2 percent and we’ve got a big balance sheet, well, why didn’t we buy a lot of assets when we cut rates to 2 percent in 2008?	96	9

201507	772	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	773	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	In preparing for this round, I, too, tried to ground my thinking in guiding principles.	96	9
201507	774	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	They’re not the same as President Rosengren’s.	96	9
201507	775	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I came up with three.	96	9
201507	776	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	First, consistency with the Policy Normalization Principles and Plans document that we published in June 2011 and updated last September.	96	9
201507	777	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	As I read it, the September 2014 document established that reductions in SOMA holdings will be done gradually and predictably, that the timing of ceasing reinvestment after liftoff will be state dependent—that is, on the economic and financial conditions and the outlook—and that it is the Committee’s desire to return to a portfolio consisting primarily of Treasury securities, implying that runoff of MBS will be part of normalization from the outset.	96	9
201507	778	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	The document also said we do not anticipate selling MBS.	96	9
201507	779	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Everybody is familiar with all of those principles.	96	9
201507	780	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	My second guideline is that our reinvestment policy should, broadly speaking, work in support of interest rate policy in pursuit of our dual-mandate objectives.	96	9
201507	781	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	This could be turned around to mean that reinvestment policy should not work counter to interest rate policy.	96	9
201507	782	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	My third principle is, the approach should be simple, uncomplicated, and clear in the substance of policy and its communication.	96	9
201507	783	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	In other words, I don’t think our reinvestment approach should risk being too cute.	96	9
201507	784	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	In the spirit of this go-round, my thinking on the questions is preliminary, not as developed as many of the people who went ahead of me.	96	9
201507	785	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I lean in favor of what I consider a simple approach with these elements:  First, make the decision on the timing of ceasing reinvestments once the mechanics of ongoing interest rate policy implementation have been operationalized and are running smoothly.	96	9
201507	786	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Second, I do prefer a qualitative, state-dependent guidance approach.	96	9
201507	787	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Set the timing of starting cessation of reinvestment in light of economic conditions once we’re reasonably confident the economy can handle any additional tightening that might come from balance sheet reductions.	96	9
201507	788	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Third, allow full passive runoff.	96	9
201507	789	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Even though reductions will vary over time, a published maturity schedule should satisfy the predictability criterion.	96	9
201507	790	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	And review the approach periodically in an attempt to assess considerations such as coherence with the expected path of interest rate policy, the extent the variable schedule of reductions is affecting the potency of interest rate policy, and any effect on market functioning.	96	9
201507	791	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	The Committee does have other options, as already discussed, of course.	96	9
201507	792	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	For example, monthly reduction could be set as a straight line of equal monthly increments.	96	9
201507	793	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	The mix between Treasuries and MBS could be altered.	96	9
201507	794	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We’ve discussed the pros and cons of this idea before.	96	9
201507	795	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	And it’s possible to imagine a scheme of tight coordination between interest rate and balance sheet normalization, trying to integrate these two tools into a dynamically set, data-dependent overall policy stance.	96	9
201507	796	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m not warm to these ideas.	96	9
201507	797	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	At present, I’m concerned that over-engineering might produce communication and other issues.	96	9
201507	798	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	So, at this point, I prefer keeping it simple.	96	9
201507	799	2015-07-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9

201507	805	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	I found it quite helpful.	96	9
201507	806	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	I, like President Lockhart, start with our normalization principles.	96	9
201507	807	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Our September 2014 principles provide some guidance on how the Committee will handle its portfolio, including reducing its size and returning its composition to primarily Treasury securities.	96	9
201507	808	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	We stated in the principles that we plan to reduce the balance sheet in a gradual and predictable manner, primarily by ending reinvestments, that reinvestments will end sometime after we begin raising the federal funds rate, and that the precise timing will depend on how the economy and outlook evolve.	96	9
201507	809	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Whatever plan we choose should be consistent with these principles.	96	9
201507	810	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	My preference is also to adopt a simple approach, because at this point I don’t see any clear benefits to adopting a more complicated one.	96	9
201507	811	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	I think the main issues are determining the starting point for ending reinvestments and determining when to communicate our strategy.	96	9
201507	812	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	While I would like the balance sheet to return to a more normal size and composition, I don’t see a compelling reason to begin this in the very early stages of liftoff.	96	9
201507	813	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	I’d rather the balance sheet remain passive for a time after liftoff, so that we don’t encourage the idea that the balance sheet, in addition to interest rates, is a regular or active tool of monetary policy.	96	9
201507	814	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	We’ve stated that we’ll time the end of reinvestments based on the economy.	96	9
201507	815	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	So the further in advance we want to communicate something more concrete about our reinvestment strategy, the less reasonable a calendar-based strategy is, because we don’t know precisely how the economy will evolve.	96	9
201507	816	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	That leaves a state-dependent strategy.	96	9
201507	817	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Now, one reason I don’t think the balance sheet should be viewed as a regular tool of monetary policy is that I don’t believe we have estimates of its effect on risk premiums and the real economy that are precise enough to be able to use it in that way.	96	9
201507	818	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	This argues for not setting separate economic conditions for ending reinvestments.	96	9
201507	819	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	My preference would be, for at least around this table, to think about ending reinvestments tied to the federal funds rate.	96	9
201507	820	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Essentially, this means that the economic conditions for ending reinvestments are the same ones we’ll be using to determine the appropriate target for the funds rate.	96	9
201507	821	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Participants who’ve said today that they would be comfortable beginning reinvestments after a couple of federal funds rate increases are essentially doing this.	96	9
201507	822	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	The staff memo illustrates a scenario in which reinvestments stop when the federal funds rate hits 2 percent.	96	9
201507	823	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Under the Tealbook baseline, this means full reinvestments continue for almost two years after liftoff.	96	9
201507	824	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	That’s too long.	96	9
201507	825	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	I’d be much more comfortable ending reinvestments sooner—say, when the fund rate is up to 1 percent.	96	9
201507	826	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	If the balance sheet effects are larger than we thought, then we could adjust the subsequent path of the funds rate after the end of reinvestments to take account of that.	96	9
201507	827	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	If an adverse shock were to hit the economy so that the federal funds rate needs to move back down, we could begin reinvestments again if need be.	96	9
201507	828	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	One issue that was not raised in the memo is when to convey information to the public about our reinvestment strategy.	96	9
201507	829	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	While market participants are likely to turn attention to reinvestments once we lift off—indeed, there’s already some discussion of this by market participants and Fed watchers—I’m not convinced that at liftoff or shortly thereafter we need to say much more about our reinvestment strategy than we’ve already said in the normalization principles and what will be conveyed in the minutes of this meeting.	96	9
201507	830	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	It would be useful to get the Desk’s view on how much advance notice market participants really need in order to prepare for the end of reinvestment.	96	9
201507	831	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	At some point after we’ve had experience with raising the federal funds rate, we would announce our reinvestment strategy.	96	9
201507	832	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	If the market doesn’t need much advance notice to prepare, then the Committee could introduce statement language saying that if the economy evolves as expected, then we plan to end reinvestments at the next meeting, or at the time of the next federal funds rate increase.	96	9
201507	833	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	We could presage this intention a meeting or two beforehand, similar to what we did when we began reducing our third LSAP program in December 2013.	96	9
201507	834	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	You may recall that at the September 2013 meeting, the Committee introduced language saying that the economic improvement since the start of the purchase program was consistent with underlying strength in the economy, but that the Committee decided to wait for more evidence that the progress was sustainable before adjusting the pace of purchases.	96	9
201507	835	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	It repeated this language in October, and then tapering commenced in December.	96	9
201507	836	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	So we could use a similar approach here if we thought that it was important to give some advance notice.	96	9
201507	837	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Finally, with regard to whether to end reinvestments completely or phase them out over time, and whether to treat Treasuries or MBS differently, my initial thought is to keep it simple, like President Lockhart, by ending reinvestments all at once and treating Treasury securities and MBS in the same way.	96	9
201507	838	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	The pattern of redemptions already has some phaseout built in.	96	9
201507	839	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	The macroeconomic effects will be the same whether we announce reinvestments are ending completely or whether we announce a path of gradual phaseout.	96	9
201507	840	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	And as the staff memo indicated, market functioning was not adversely affected by the end of our first LSAP program in March 2010, when the SOMA net purchases of MBS fell more than $40 billion.	96	9
201507	841	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Indeed, ending reinvestments might aid market functioning because it will mean there will be more safe assets available for collateral and repo in the hands of the public.	96	9
201507	842	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	In addition, market participants know the CUSIPs in our SOMA portfolio.	96	9
201507	843	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	So once we announce when reinvestments will end, they’ll know the path of Treasury redemptions, and they’ll be able to estimate the path of MBS redemptions.	96	9
201507	844	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	That said, the MBS market has changed over time, and the Desk estimates that MBS prepayments are expected to be about 30 percent of TBA gross issuance in 2016, requiring the private sector to absorb a large portion of the market.	96	9
201507	845	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Further analysis by the Desk of the risks of ending reinvestments all at once, rather than phasing them out, would be helpful.	96	9
201507	846	2015-07-29	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	847	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201507	848	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Fischer.	96	9
201507	849	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	850	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	When I first started thinking about when to cease reinvestments, my instinct was that we should decide based on current and expected economic conditions.	96	9
201507	851	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	After all, the size of the balance sheet is a monetary policy tool, and so it should be chosen in the same deliberate and comprehensive way in which we make federal funds rate decisions, or that we used to purchase the assets in the first place through our various QE programs.	96	9
201507	852	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	So I was fundamentally in the state-based camp, and I wanted not to tie us down too much before it was necessary.	96	9
201507	853	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	However, the more I thought about it, the more I realized that a lot depends on how powerful the effects of announcing the dates and conditions for the end of reinvestments will be.	96	9
201507	854	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	To a first approximation—maybe a bad one, but it’s an approximation—one can say that announcing the schedule for sales, when it comes, will be equivalent to a given basis point increase or decrease—I’ll explain that in a minute—in the federal funds rate.	96	9
201507	855	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	But that isn’t quite right.	96	9
201507	856	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	The markets have an expectation of how large the balance sheet will be at each future date.	96	9
201507	857	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	If our announcement is that we’re going to go early relative to those dates, we’ll be tightening.	96	9
201507	858	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	If we go late relative to those dates, we’ll be easing.	96	9
201507	859	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	Further, if the markets have reasonable foresight, we get most of the reaction with the announcement, and then carrying it out doesn’t have as much effect as one thinks.	96	9
201507	860	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	The less foresight people have, the more one has to take into account all of the effects that President Rosengren indicated a few minutes ago.	96	9
201507	861	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I think, at the very general level, our principle is that we should go late with the announcement and with the beginning of the running off the portfolio.	96	9
201507	862	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I say that because I think that the main thing we’ve got to avoid is getting back to the zero lower bound.	96	9
201507	863	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	One of you said that we want to go up using the two tools so we get to an interest rate that will make us feel comfortable about not going back.	96	9
201507	864	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	Now, let’s go to the key point.	96	9
201507	865	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	How big will these effects be?	96	9
201507	866	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I was surprised to hear President Rosengren talk about a 75 basis point effect, measured in terms of an equivalent move in the federal funds rate, of some aspect of phasing.	96	9
201507	867	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’ve seen no evidence that we’ll be anywhere near as powerful as that in the timing of selling off different parts of the portfolio.	96	9
201507	868	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’m not quite sure of the empirical significance of the lower right-hand chart in exhibit 1 of the handout that we got on SOMA reinvestment policy, but it does suggest that waiting a year doesn’t make much of a difference to interest rates at any time.	96	9
201507	869	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I also think I’ve read a paper or heard a statement indicating that the effect of the running off the portfolio will be in the direction we all believe—namely, that a larger portfolio is more expansionary, but that the size of the effects will be relatively small.	96	9
201507	870	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I think we have to ask the staff to tell us how powerful this is.	96	9
201507	871	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	If the whole thing is worth the equivalent of 25 basis points in running down from $4 billion to $1 billion, that’s not huge.	96	9
201507	872	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	One is tempted to say, “Well, we should just reverse the results of our empirical work on the effect of quantitative easing—unless there’s quantitative lack of easing—and then we’ll get the right answer.”	96	9
201507	873	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	But there’s so much expectation in these things regarding what you’re saying about future policy that I’m really not sure that you could just do that reversal and say, “That’s what’s going to happen.”	96	9
201507	874	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	And the question is, what message are we sending now?	96	9
201507	875	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’d announce the beginning of the nonreinvestments relatively late to give us a safety cushion with regard to going back to zero, which I think for a variety of reasons is a problem.	96	9
201507	876	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I agree with those people who’ve said we really don’t want to go there.	96	9
201507	877	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	And the reason I reached that conclusion even before this discussion was, I’ve hardly heard anybody say around this table when bad news comes in, “Okay, guys, let’s do another QE.”	96	9
201507	878	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	In fact, it seems to have just fallen off the table, and I assume that reflects the conclusions we’ve all arrived at.	96	9
201507	879	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	If these effects are powerful, we’re going to have to have some more work by the staff telling us how to coordinate these two instruments.	96	9
201507	880	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	What do we expect when we sell off at a given rate?	96	9
201507	881	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	If we expect very little effect, we don’t have to worry very much, and we can just fix it.	96	9
201507	882	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	If it’s powerful, then we’re going to have to think about what we’re doing at each stage.	96	9
201507	883	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	In the end, because I believe the effects are relatively small, I’ll end up with quite a few of you.	96	9
201507	884	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’d give President Lockhart the prize for the most apt analogy in this FOMC meeting.	96	9
201507	885	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’ve never thought of programs for reinvestment as being cute, but I’m very pleased to think about it.	96	9
201507	886	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	We don’t want to be too cute if it isn’t that important.	96	9
201507	887	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	If it is that important, we’ll have to be a little cuter, and then go into all of the elements that President Rosengren—and, I think to some extent, Governor Tarullo—mentioned.	96	9
201507	888	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	Again, whether that very sophisticated analysis you gave, Governor Tarullo, is going to be the essence of what we do, or an aspect of what we do, depends on just how powerful this tool is that we’re going to be using.	96	9
201507	889	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	So what I’d like to ask for is that the staff come back with some quantitative stories about what will happen, or what they expect will happen, or the range of things that could happen, depending on the strategies.	96	9
201507	890	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	If you can say this doesn’t matter at all, then we could do it on other grounds.	96	9
201507	891	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	If you say this really matters, then we’ll have to do a lot more thinking.	96	9
201507	892	2015-07-29	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9

201507	894	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	96	9
201507	895	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	896	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	I prefer the qualitative state-dependent approach to initiating changes to our reinvestment policies.	96	9
201507	897	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	However, once we start, I think there should be a high hurdle for making changes in the pace of our balance sheet reductions.	96	9
201507	898	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	Before we being altering our reinvestments, I think we should be well under way in the funds rate normalization process, and I think this is the biggest issue.	96	9
201507	899	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	I think a lot of what we’re talking about comes down to this:  We don’t know the effect of the balance sheet adjustments and how they are going to affect longer-term rates, and that translates into some equivalent increase in the funds rate.	96	9
201507	900	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	If we get to a point at which the funds rate is high enough, there’s some offset that can be done with the funds rate itself or the funds rate path trajectory— somebody said this earlier as well.	96	9
201507	901	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	So once we get to the point when the funds rate is a viable separate tool, I think it takes care of a lot of these issues.	96	9
201507	902	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	By that time, I expect everything should be working smoothly, with a strong economic outlook and inflation rising toward 2 percent.	96	9
201507	903	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	I thought Governor Tarullo’s comments on the Bank of England guidance along these lines of the policy rate being high enough were particularly appropriate and helpful.	96	9
201507	904	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	At that point, we should follow through on our stated goal of returning to a traditional policy environment in which adjusting the funds rate is our primary tool for monetary policy.	96	9
201507	905	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	This would mean putting our balance sheet reductions on “cruise control” as much as possible.	96	9
201507	906	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	We should do this in accordance with our exit-principles statement that we will reduce security holdings in a gradual and predictable manner.	96	9
201507	907	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	I hope we won’t need to adjust our reinvestment policies regularly, and certainly not as another policy lever, if things are going well.	96	9
201507	908	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	This means that before we begin to cease reinvestments, we ought to be reasonably confident that we will be able to adequately respond to future shocks through adjustments in the funds rate.	96	9
201507	909	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	This judgment regarding how high the funds rate needs to be before we alter our reinvestments is going to depend on the evolution of the economic environment and undoubtedly will have an aspect of “we’ll know it when we see it.”	96	9
201507	910	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	This leads me to think that the best starting rule for ending reinvestments is one that is qualitative and state dependent.	96	9
201507	911	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	On the other questions, I defer judgment to the Desk on how best to engineer the gradual and predictable reduction in the balance sheet.	96	9
201507	912	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	From the memo, I infer that the Desk would prefer to taper reinvestments, at least for a while, to insure against market disruption.	96	9
201507	913	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	I’m fine with this at the start and understand that we may have to treat MBS differently from Treasury securities.	96	9
201507	914	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	But we should communicate that any decisions regarding the tapering process are dictated by market-microstructure and potential market dislocation considerations and not by macroeconomic monetary policy concerns.	96	9
201507	915	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	We don’t want markets to confuse technical adjustments with changes in the stance of monetary policy.	96	9
201507	916	2015-07-29	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9

201507	919	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Perhaps just as a brief clarification, because there have been some questions about our estimate of the size of the macroeconomic effects of these changes in reinvestment strategies.	96	9
201507	920	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Beth’s handout was only showing the comparison of the path for the federal funds rate.	96	9

201507	923	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	When you then go to page 15 of the memo, you see roughly what the effect of that is.	96	9
201507	924	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	For example, on the unemployment rate, it’s roughly on the order of 0.1 percentage point at its peak.	96	9
201507	925	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	So after a couple of years, the unemployment rate is about 0.1 percentage point lower.	96	9
201507	926	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Now, again, the point applies that President Lacker made beforehand—namely, in principle, of course, you could adjust the federal funds rate so as to completely insulate.	96	9
201507	927	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	So if you started off with some path of the unemployment rate that you had previously determined to be optimal, you could, away from the zero lower bound, adjust the funds rate so as to insulate the economy completely from any changes in reinvestment strategy.	96	9
201507	928	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	But just to provide an order of magnitude, if you chose the differences in the path of the SOMA holdings and funds rate as shown in the memo, then that would be the resulting maximum effect on the unemployment rate.	96	9
201507	929	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	So that’s in FRB/US?	96	9

201507	932	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	In particular, of course, it relies on the staff’s methodology that the effects result primarily from the stock of our holdings, and are being transmitted through term premiums as we estimate them.	96	9
201507	933	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	I will readily admit that there is a lot of uncertainty about that.	96	9

201507	937	2015-07-29	meeting	DUDLEY	You’re then forestalling all those paths where you would’ve kept the balance sheet higher for a much longer period of time, and that’s not really captured completely in the model because the model is based on creating one path.	96	9

201507	965	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Much of that adjustment had to do with the difficulty of estimating how asset prices other than, for example, 10-year term premiums respond.	96	9

201507	967	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Subsequently, we thought we observed somewhat smaller asset price responses like the stock market and, therefore, scaled back.	96	9
201507	968	2015-07-29	meeting	POTTER	So one thing we could do is calibrate under those different responses so you could see that.	96	9
201507	969	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Okay.	96	9

201507	976	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201507	977	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	As others have said, I believe that once we’ve achieved a degree of comfort regarding our ability to control short-term market rates, we should begin to reduce the size of our balance sheet.	96	9
201507	978	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	I see little reason to decide today when that will be.	96	9
201507	979	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	In my view, the process that governs the shrinking of the balance sheet should be simple, straightforward, and kept, as President Mester said, distinct from direct adjustments to monetary policy accomplished through changes in the federal funds rate target.	96	9
201507	980	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	It should be calendar based, I believe, but at a date announced after liftoff when we are confident that we are well away from the lower bound.	96	9
201507	981	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	It should be independent of economic conditions, and reductions in the balance sheet should proceed at a fairly constant pace.	96	9
201507	982	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	To avoid the volatility associated with simply ceasing reinvestments, we can, for example—and as others have mentioned—choose a pace that reduces the amount of longer-term Treasury securities and MBS at somewhat less than the average value of anticipated monthly reinvestments.	96	9
201507	983	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	Doing so would involve outright sales in some months and reinvestments in other months in order to hit the preset target.	96	9
201507	984	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	Proceeding in this manner would make the evolution of our portfolio transparent and avoid the complications that would accompany treating portfolio adjustments as a complementary tool of policy.	96	9
201507	985	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	There’s too much uncertainty surrounding the effects of balance sheet manipulation to treat the normalization of the balance sheet in a way that mimics the normalization of our primary policy instrument, in my opinion.	96	9
201507	986	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	This ends my attempt to answer the questions posed to us.	96	9
201507	987	2015-07-29	meeting	HARKER	President Williams, consider this my rookie mistake.	96	9
