201507	2537	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	So it may not be as revealing of underlying wage trends as some of the other measures.	13	1
201507	2538	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Indeed, I was thinking this weekend—in the inevitable seven- to eight-week effort to ask, “What can you say that’s new?”—that I actually now believe that the story of wages in this recovery was written by Samuel Beckett.	13	1
201507	2539	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	This is not an overly literary crowd, I can tell.	13	1
201507	2540	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	[Laughter]	13	1
201507	2541	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	But I will now elaborate, although I appreciate that the Chair got it.	13	1
201507	2542	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	It might not be a funny reference.	13	1
201507	2543	2015-07-29	meeting	LACKER	[Laughter]	13	1
201507	2544	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We’re waiting.	13	1
201507	2545	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Beckett had his boy character appear only twice to announce that Godot would not be arriving today but would surely be arriving the next day, whereas we have heard predictions of accelerating wages and anecdotal reports of same more or less continuously during the past couple of years.	13	1
201507	2546	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Now, while Godot never did arrive, sending Vladimir and Estragon to the point of suicide, most of us probably believe that accelerating wages will.	13	1
201507	2547	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	There have been numerous efforts both inside and outside the System to determine just when that might be, based on historical correlations between accelerating wage increases in post-recession periods and other labor market indicators.	13	1
201507	2548	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	I want to mention a couple of relatively recent efforts by Federal Reserve economists that I found both interesting and well thought through.	13	1
201507	2549	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	But precisely because they turn out, perhaps, not to be correct, I think they’re a cautionary tale about reading too much into any effort to create such correlations.	13	1
201507	2550	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	One, which I believe hasn’t been reduced to a paper yet but was presented within various parts of the System earlier this year, suggests that wages begin to accelerate when the post-recession unemployment rate has declined between 70 and 80 percent of the way from its recession high to its pre-recession trough.	13	1
201507	2551	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The other, which is a little less numerically determinate, maps historical correlations between the quits rate and wage increases and concludes that a rise in the former is a good predictor of a later rise in the latter.	13	1
201507	2552	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	That is a Federal Reserve Bank of Chicago Fed Letter—it was just posted on the Federal Reserve Bank of Chicago’s website.	13	1
201507	2553	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	With respect to the first, if my arithmetic is right—not always a foregone conclusion—we’ve now already retraced more than 80 percent of the increase in unemployment from the pre-recession low to the recession high without noticeable and persistent wage acceleration.	13	1
201507	2554	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	And when I looked at the charts that were presented by the authors of that presentation, by the time that 70 to 80 percent had been reached, there was already a quite persistent and noticeable increase.	13	1
201507	2555	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	With respect to quits, while the quits rate has been rising for some years now, it has only relatively recently gotten back into the lower end of its pre-crisis range.	13	1
201507	2556	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	So it may be a little bit early to judge how well this correlation holds up in the present recovery.	13	1
201507	2557	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	If I read the paper right, President Evans, I think that paper was not actually trying to make a very firm numerical determination but was instead just trying to suggest directionally that this is when you can begin to expect some acceleration of wages.	13	1
201507	2558	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	My point, as in past discussions, is that the origins of the 2007–09 recession and the ensuing recovery in a financial crisis may mean that there will be very different trajectories in the labor market, as there have been in some other areas.	13	1
201507	2559	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	So we should remain open to the possibility, even the likelihood, that things won’t be following the same pattern as they have been in the past several recessions and recoveries, and we have to instead look for nontransitory evidence in the data.	13	1
201507	2560	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	All of that, of course, is against the backdrop of the considerable uncertainty about the relationship between wage acceleration, even when it does occur, and price inflation.	13	1
201507	2561	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Turning to international factors, I want to talk about two that, again, several people have mentioned that carry some downside risk.	13	1
201507	2562	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The first is China.	13	1
201507	2563	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Now, I do not pretend to understand what is going on in China, and I certainly don’t have very much confidence in my own assessment of the risks of a significant drop-off in economic growth there.	13	1
201507	2564	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	What I’ve noticed is that people who speak to Chinese officials or who analyze data tend to discount the stock market turmoil and take a relatively optimistic view that China’s growth will stabilize around where it’s now reported to be, whereas people who do business in China tend as a group to be more pessimistic and view the overleveraged stock market as a harbinger of other problems.	13	1
201507	2565	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Being in neither group—I guess that’s not true because at FSB meetings, I talk to Chinese officials—I can readily identify cognitive biases in both groups, so I don’t know whose story is more convincing.	13	1
201507	2566	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	But what I think is relatively clear is that there isn’t much upside risk in China these days.	13	1
201507	2567	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	So, while the risks it poses to global economic growth and, through the mechanism of reduced demand for commodities, to downward pressures on inflation may be hard to quantify for now, those risks are not balanced by any realistic upside risk that, say, Chinese economic growth is going to improve to between 8 and 9 percent over the next couple of years.	13	1
201507	2568	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	On the dollar, the Tealbook already projects significant drags on US growth over the next four to six quarters stemming from negative net exports, the reasons for which Steve explained in his introductory remarks.	13	1
201507	2569	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Because the Tealbook also projects only a small additional increase in the trade-weighted value of the dollar during that period, what they’re projecting is mostly a J-curve effect.	13	1
201507	2570	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	But against the backdrop of the Tealbook’s stipulation of a September federal funds rate increase, the Tealbook projection embeds the assumption that most of the capital investment shift associated with divergent monetary policies has already been priced into relative markets.	13	1
201507	2571	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	This may well be the case, but I think there are at least some reasons to think otherwise.	13	1
201507	2572	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The first, of course, is the fact that rates have been at the zero lower bound here for more than six and a half years.	13	1
201507	2573	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	So there may have developed more entrenchment of positions that haven’t moved so much, even in response to the increasingly explicit predictions of rate rises that many have been announcing.	13	1
201507	2574	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Second, any near-term increase in US rates will have been accompanied by a decrease in effective rates in much of the rest of the world.	13	1
201507	2575	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The only clear exceptions already are South Africa and Brazil, and the United Kingdom looms out there as potentially an exception along with us.	13	1
201507	2576	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Accommodation has been enhanced significantly in both the euro zone and Japan through their QE programs.	13	1
201507	2577	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	This is a great statistic:  Rate reductions by central banks in the rest of the world have outnumbered increases 44 to 4 since the beginning of the year.	13	1
201507	2578	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The 4 are, again, 2 in South Africa and 2 in Brazil.	13	1
201507	2579	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	So I wonder whether the traditional pattern of markets buying on rumors and selling on the fact may not hold true here, and whether there may be the potential for greater cross-border capital flows if we increase rates before either economic or financial conditions have become more mixed in the rest of the world.	13	1
201507	2580	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	The risk here is, I believe, a little more balanced than that with respect to China, because, if the Greek situation continues to be a problem mostly for the Greek people and not for the rest of the euro zone, one can definitely imagine the euro strengthening somewhat.	13	1
201507	2581	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	But I think it very unlikely that there would be a significant depreciation of the dollar when we start raising rates, whereas there is at least a modest risk of a significant appreciation.	13	1
201507	2582	2015-07-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201507	2583	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201507	2584	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Powell.	13	1
201507	2585	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201507	2586	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	What have we learned since the June meeting?	13	1
201507	2587	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	I’m tempted to say, “Not much,” in light of the paucity of new US economic data in the intermeeting period.	13	1
201507	2588	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	However, the little data that we have received do support continued confidence in the trajectory of the economy.	13	1
201507	2589	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Moreover, some of the near-term uncertainties on the international environment have materially diminished.	13	1
201507	2590	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	The labor market has continued to strengthen.	13	1
201507	2591	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Payrolls averaged 220,000 per month in the second quarter.	13	1
201507	2592	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	The unemployment rate dropped to 5.3 percent in June and now is 0.3 percentage point below last December’s reading, although some of that is probably due to the 0.3 percentage point drop in the labor force participation rate in June, which it may well reverse—I certainly hope that it does.	13	1
201507	2593	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Nonetheless, labor market slack continues to diminish.	13	1
201507	2594	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	I have a comment on the box on pages 20–21 of Tealbook A.	13	1
201507	2595	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	The box, on employment and unemployment in the staff projection, describes a pro-cyclical relationship between the different measures of employment in the establishment survey as compared with the household survey.	13	1
201507	2596	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	That difference is a big part of what’s driving the baseline forecast of a significant slowdown in the pace of decline of U-3 in the household survey in the face of still-strong payroll growth.	13	1
201507	2597	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	So it’s a very important box, and I applaud its inclusion in the Tealbook.	13	1
201507	2598	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	As the box says, this pro-cyclical relationship has held somewhat consistently, but not totally consistently, across prior recoveries, and I continue to think that there’s a significant chance that U-3 will decline faster and reach a lower level than the forecast shows, given payroll growth.	13	1
201507	2599	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	We also now have more evidence that the stalling of GDP in the first quarter was anomalous.	13	1
201507	2600	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	In addition, some of the real weakness in the first half came from the drop in oilfield investment, and the recent bottoming out in oil rig counts indicates that the substantial drag from that sector may have run its course.	13	1
201507	2601	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Although the recent further decline in oil prices may spur a bit more of a pullback, I don’t expect that it will be as extreme as what we’ve just been through.	13	1
201507	2602	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	So the second half should be stronger than the first.	13	1
201507	2603	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	The staff’s second-half GDP forecast is notably more downbeat than that of private forecasters, most of whom seem to be at 2½ percent or above.	13	1
201507	2604	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	David Wilcox noted earlier that that was principally due, we think, to net exports.	13	1
201507	2605	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	We’re not submitting a real GDP growth forecast for this round, but I feel that, at a minimum, there’s risk to the upside.	13	1
201507	2606	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	I want to stop there for a second and echo what Governor Tarullo said earlier.	13	1
201507	2607	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	I’ve chosen, with some trepidation, to depart from the staff forecast on a couple of items.	13	1
201507	2608	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	I want to say that I appreciate that what you do is to take a position, explain it with great transparency, and not be too concerned about where the public consensus is.	13	1
201507	2609	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Then you grade yourself in the back of the book and show how the actual performance was.	13	1
201507	2610	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	I think there’s a lot of value in that, and I appreciate the thoughtfulness that goes into it.	13	1
201507	2611	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	One of the risks to economic growth that was frequently noted in the last go-round in June was the disruptions from developments in Greece and China, and those risks do seem much lower now, as has been noted by many around the table.	13	1
201507	2612	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	There’s been no important fallout to date from the ongoing Chinese stock market correction.	13	1
201507	2613	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Greece now seems to be headed toward a new deal with its creditors and not to an exit.	13	1
201507	2614	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Even if that deal doesn’t get done, the measures taken over the past several years in Europe seem to have successfully inoculated the periphery from contagion from Greece.	13	1
201507	2615	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	So it seems to me that the risks to our economy from international developments have diminished materially since the June meeting.	13	1
201507	2616	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	An additional risk I mentioned earlier is the risk that the expectation and reality of increasing policy rates in the United States will cause the dollar to strengthen more than forecast, causing a further decline in net exports as demand is shifted abroad.	13	1
201507	2617	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Unfortunately, this risk seems likely to be with us as long as global economic growth remains weak, and the sharp decline in commodity prices does suggest that that could be a while.	13	1
201507	2618	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Turning to inflation, the other half of our mandate:  The price and wage data clearly present some challenges.	13	1
201507	2619	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	The staff estimates that total PCE inflation was only 0.2 percent for the 12 months ending in June, and that core inflation was only 1¼ percent.	13	1
201507	2620	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Of course, headline inflation is being pulled down by oil prices, and that will end.	13	1
201507	2621	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	The staff estimates that core inflation is also being held down about 40 basis points by the indirect effects of energy and import prices.	13	1
201507	2622	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	That would suggest that underlying core inflation may be around 1.7 percent.	13	1
201507	2623	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	It therefore seems to me reasonable to expect, with some degree of confidence, that core and total inflation will move back up to 1¾ percent once these temporary factors are behind us.	13	1
201507	2624	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	However, the recent decline in oil prices and the appreciation of the dollar will restrain inflation throughout the second half of this year and, to a much lesser extent, next year, and that may present a real communications challenge throughout the fall as the Committee considers liftoff.	13	1
201507	2625	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	A related challenge comes from the wage data.	13	1
201507	2626	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Wage pressures are everywhere in the anecdotes but still not that easy to find in the data.	13	1
201507	2627	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	Average hourly earnings, the most prominent wage measure, rose only 2 percent over the 12 months ending in June.	13	1
201507	2628	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	By contrast, as others have noted, the ECI is now at 2.6 percent over the trailing 12 months, although, as President Rosengren and others have mentioned, there are reasons to doubt the sustainability of that measure.	13	1
201507	2629	2015-07-29	meeting	POWELL	We’re going to get several readings on labor compensation before the September meeting—including another ECI, average hourly earnings, and compensation per hour—which may help clarify our assessment of labor market conditions as well as ease the challenge of communicating that assessment.	13	1

201507	2632	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	13	1
201507	2633	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201507	2634	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The data since June have contained few surprises on the domestic front, although the price of oil is down about 20 percent and the exchange rate is up an additional 3 percent since then.	13	1
201507	2635	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I want to underscore the observation made earlier that, while we have seen a welcome return to moderate economic growth in the second quarter, we have not seen a bounceback sufficient to compensate for the slowdown in the first quarter relative to what had been anticipated.	13	1
201507	2636	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The labor market has continued to improve steadily.	13	1
201507	2637	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Consumption remains moderate, buoyed by strong fundamentals, but apparently not strong enough to overcome the continued drag on investment and production from earlier oil price declines and the persistent effects of a stronger exchange rate.	13	1
201507	2638	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Inflation remains noticeably and persistently below our 2 percent target.	13	1
201507	2639	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Let me take each of those in turn.	13	1
201507	2640	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The current data suggest that net exports subtracted a little over 1 percentage point from GDP growth over the first half of this year, and the staff’s econometric model suggests that trade will continue to exert substantial downward pressure on demand through 2016.	13	1
201507	2641	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Given this restraint and the relatively moderate pace of increase in domestic demand, increases in overall demand are likely to remain quite limited.	13	1
201507	2642	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Although there are numerous factors supporting consumer demand—rising real income, high net worth, and buoyant sentiment—the recent data continue to suggest that consumer spending is rising at a relatively moderate pace of around 3 percent over the middle of the year.	13	1
201507	2643	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The recent data on housing starts and permits point to further gains in residential investment, but the rise in activity remains gradual and the contribution to overall demand relatively modest.	13	1
201507	2644	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The drag on business investment due to last year’s sharp decline in oil prices looks to be fading, with the sharp fall in drilling rigs over the first half of this year leveling out.	13	1
201507	2645	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Even so, new orders for capital goods and measures of business sentiment suggest fairly tepid increases in investment spending over the second half of this year, and the implications of the recent drop in oil prices are as yet unclear.	13	1
201507	2646	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Meanwhile, government spending looks to add very little to aggregate demand growth this year.	13	1
201507	2647	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The pace of improvement in the labor market has been stronger than that for aggregate demand for some time, with the difference being reflected in strikingly weak measured productivity growth.	13	1
201507	2648	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The labor market improvement has been steady but somewhat more gradual so far this year.	13	1
201507	2649	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The sizable decrease in the overall unemployment rate in the July report was offset by a decline in labor force participation; it also came with a somewhat surprising drop in average hourly earnings growth.	13	1
201507	2650	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Job gains have clearly slowed from last year’s very rapid pace.	13	1
201507	2651	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Looking at a wide range of labor market indicators suggests to me that some slack still remains, even with overall unemployment at 5.3 percent.	13	1
201507	2652	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Recent demographic changes and other structural changes in the labor market, as well as still-subdued wage growth, suggest that the natural rate could be below the current level of the unemployment rate.	13	1
201507	2653	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	As has been discussed at some length, slack also exists on the labor force participation margin.	13	1
201507	2654	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Despite some cyclical improvement over the past year or so, the participation rate remains below what I believe to be its structural trend.	13	1
201507	2655	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The number of those out of the labor force but wanting a job, as well as other measures of marginally attached nonparticipants, still appears elevated relative to pre-recession norms, and the same is true of the share of employees working part time for economic reasons.	13	1
201507	2656	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	That said, the labor market certainly continues to show improvement.	13	1
201507	2657	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	In contrast, incoming data so far have not provided grounds for reasonable confidence on the inflation leg of our dual mandate.	13	1
201507	2658	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The recent data suggest an underlying trend of price inflation of around 1¼ to 1½ percent.	13	1
201507	2659	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The 12-month change in core PCE prices, for example, is estimated to have been 1¼ percent in June, while the 12-month change in the Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas trimmed mean was 1½ percent in May.	13	1
201507	2660	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	These rates are quite similar to the 1¼ percent average pace of core inflation over the past several years.	13	1
201507	2661	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	As the effect of dollar appreciation on core import prices fades and resource utilization tightens further, I would expect that inflation will rise toward our 2 percent target.	13	1
201507	2662	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	But, in view of the absence of any noticeable response of inflation to the reduction in resource slack over the past several years and the apparent flattening of the Phillips curve, the increase is likely to be quite gradual.	13	1
201507	2663	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Furthermore, the risks to the inflation forecast seem to be tilted to the downside.	13	1
201507	2664	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Although inflation expectations have been quite stable, there are some hints of some movement downward.	13	1
201507	2665	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	This is true if you look at market-based inflation expectations; we’re also seeing that in survey measures.	13	1
201507	2666	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	As I mentioned earlier, we’ve seen a further leg down in crude oil prices and some increase in the trade-weighted dollar.	13	1
201507	2667	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	There’s also a fair risk that the downward pressure on inflation due to dollar appreciation and falling commodity prices could stretch beyond this year.	13	1
201507	2668	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	This last concern follows from the foreign economic outlook.	13	1
201507	2669	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	China is slowing to an unknown degree and exerting a drag on both commodity prices and the growth prospects of commodity exporters.	13	1
201507	2670	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Although reported Chinese GDP growth was surprisingly robust in the second quarter following relatively weak first-quarter growth, the extent to which this may reflect a temporary run-up in the financial sector that is already reversing is unclear.	13	1
201507	2671	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Other indicators, such as commodity prices and economic growth in other East Asian economies, suggest a slowing in Chinese economic growth sufficient to exert a drag more globally.	13	1
201507	2672	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Meanwhile, economic difficulties in other important emerging markets, such as Brazil and Russia, are likely to continue for some time.	13	1
201507	2673	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	A number of our close trade partners, such as Canada and Mexico, have also slowed.	13	1
201507	2674	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The departure of Greece from the euro zone was avoided this month, so I see less risk as being associated with those scenarios.	13	1
201507	2675	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	But, of course, negotiations on a third program are likely to be contentious, and Greek economic progress is likely to be limited over the next year.	13	1
201507	2676	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	More broadly, uncertainty and weak internal demands seem likely to weigh on economic activity within the euro area, ensuring that monetary policy will stay extremely accommodative throughout the medium term, and that any contribution of Europe to global demand will remain pretty limited.	13	1
201507	2677	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	For all of those reasons, I expect foreign developments to continue to exert deflationary pressures.	13	1
201507	2678	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	As the contrast between a US economy on the verge of raising short-term rates and foreign economies in which monetary accommodation is likely to continue becomes increasingly apparent to market participants, the risks of further dollar appreciation may well increase.	13	1
201507	2679	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	As markets adjust to relatively weak demand growth in both advanced and emerging economies, global deflationary pressures could be quite persistent.	13	1
201507	2680	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	An economic outlook featuring moderate US demand growth, still-present economic slack, persistently below-target inflation, and downside risks from abroad has important implications for monetary policy, which we will return to in tomorrow’s meeting.	13	1
201507	2681	2015-07-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201507	2682	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201507	2683	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	My thanks to everyone for another interesting round of comments on the economic outlook.	13	1
201507	2684	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We’ve been at it a long time today, so I’m going to dispense with my usual summary.	13	1
201507	2685	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Today I’d just like to make a couple of comments of my own.	13	1
201507	2686	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	For me, the data flow during the intermeeting period will be critical in deciding whether it’s appropriate to raise the funds rate target range in September.	13	1
201507	2687	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	So I thought I’d comment on what I’ll be looking for in judging whether our two liftoff conditions have been met.	13	1
201507	2688	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Starting with the labor market, in my view, conditions have clearly improved somewhat since earlier in the year when we set out as a condition for liftoff that we need to see further improvement in the labor market.	13	1
201507	2689	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Based on your comments, I think this view was pretty widely shared.	13	1
201507	2690	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	The unemployment rate is down from 5.5 percent at the time of our March meeting to 5.3 percent in the June report, and the improvement in broader measures of labor utilization has been more noticeable, with U-6 down from 11 percent to 10½ percent now.	13	1
201507	2691	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	The labor force participation rate is down a bit since the March meeting, and the employment-to-population ratio is unchanged, but the sideways movement of the employment-to-population ratio represents an improvement on the underlying demographic trend.	13	1
201507	2692	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	So the staff estimates that the cyclical component of this ratio has narrowed modestly over the past four months.	13	1
201507	2693	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Payroll gains have averaged almost 200,000 per month in the four labor market reports we received since the March meeting.	13	1
201507	2694	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	That’s down considerably from the large gains seen, on average, over the previous 12 months, but the recent pace is nonetheless healthy.	13	1
201507	2695	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	If it’s maintained over the next few months, that’s consistent with a further modest rise in labor utilization.	13	1
201507	2696	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, not all of the labor market indicators are better.	13	1
201507	2697	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	The JOLTS quits rate has moved sideways, and the hiring rate is actually down a bit relative to the data we had in hand back in March.	13	1
201507	2698	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	The ECI released in April suggested a pickup in wage growth.	13	1
201507	2699	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We’ve had a very interesting discussion around the table, and, of course, as President Rosengren noted, there are a lot of question marks about how to interpret this reading, in view of the fact that the pickup is concentrated in the Northeast.	13	1
201507	2700	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	June’s disappointing reading on average hourly earnings also calls into question whether any pickup in wage gains is actually under way.	13	1
201507	2701	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Even so, not every indicator needs to move in the right direction for us to reasonably say that overall conditions have improved.	13	1
201507	2702	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	In that regard, the labor market conditions index, prepared by the Board’s staff, has registered gains in recent months.	13	1
201507	2703	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	The real issue is not whether there has been some improvement since March, but rather whether there’s been enough to justify liftoff.	13	1
201507	2704	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Personally, I think waiting until we’ve seen some further improvement is advisable, but I also believe that we could have sufficient evidence in hand by the time of the September meeting.	13	1
201507	2705	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	For example, if monthly payroll gains in July and August come in around 200,000 or so, on average—perhaps accompanied by a rise in labor force participation—I would likely judge the cumulative improvement to be sufficient.	13	1
201507	2706	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, stronger readings on average hourly earnings and the ECI would strengthen the case for me.	13	1
201507	2707	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	To be clear, I would not see such a limited amount of additional improvement as sufficient to return us to full employment.	13	1
201507	2708	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Like the staff and many of you, I believe that we still have a ways to go beyond what is likely to be accomplished in the next couple of months.	13	1
201507	2709	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We aren’t that far off anymore, and, provided that the outlook for economic growth is sufficiently strong to support a continued tightening of the labor market, I wouldn’t see a problem with starting the normalization process before all slack in the economy has been eliminated.	13	1
201507	2710	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	This economic growth requirement also bears on the other criterion we established for liftoff.	13	1
201507	2711	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	So let me next turn to the conditions that will allow me to be reasonably confident that inflation will return to 2 percent over the next few years.	13	1
201507	2712	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Inflation data over the past few months have been in line with staff projections and my own expectations.	13	1
201507	2713	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	As many of you noted, these data serve to confirm our assessment that the downward pressure on inflation stemming from the huge earlier fall in energy prices would prove to be temporary and indirectly support our assessment that the effects of past dollar appreciation will also fade.	13	1
201507	2714	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	In the meantime, however, oil prices have fallen some more, leading the staff to revise down its forecast for inflation appreciably in the second half of the year and, especially, in the fourth quarter.	13	1
201507	2715	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thus, we will face a communications challenge if we choose to lift off this year because headline PCE inflation on a 12-month basis is likely to remain close to zero until early 2016.	13	1
201507	2716	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	And, as David showed, referencing core inflation may not be of much help either, as the staff projects the available readings on 12-month core PCE inflation to continue to run close to 1¼ percent through the December meeting.	13	1
201507	2717	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	At liftoff, we will need to make a good case for projecting that inflation is heading back to 2 percent.	13	1
201507	2718	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	To me, that case largely rests on the basic nature of the inflation process.	13	1
201507	2719	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Based on the econometric evidence, I’m persuaded that something like the staff’s inflation model provides a reasonable way to assess the outlook.	13	1
201507	2720	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	According to this model, inflation should move back up to 2 percent over the medium term and in an environment of full employment, provided that longer-run inflation expectations remain anchored at their pre-crisis level and we don’t experience further significant price shocks.	13	1
201507	2721	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Most of the more complicated, DSGE, models maintained around the System make the same prediction and for essentially the same reasons.	13	1
201507	2722	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	In these models, longer-run expectations serve as an attractor to which inflation converges in the absence of offsetting pressures.	13	1
201507	2723	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, there’s a lot we don’t understand about the inflation process.	13	1
201507	2724	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	All of these models may be wrong or incomplete in some important way, but that’s true of any model.	13	1
201507	2725	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	I think the appropriate standard to apply here is not that we have complete confidence in our models, but rather that our models do a reasonably good job of explaining the historical data and are not outperformed by some other forecasting procedure with a significantly different outlook.	13	1
201507	2726	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	I believe that’s the case.	13	1
201507	2727	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Now, the staff’s estimates suggest that current survey measures of longer-run inflation expectations are not, in fact, consistent with inflation converging not to 2 percent, but instead to a modestly lower level.	13	1
201507	2728	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	If so, I would see that as roughly equivalent to saying that the natural rate of unemployment is somewhat lower than our current estimate, a possibility we always face due to the uncertain nature of our supply-side estimates.	13	1
201507	2729	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We deal with such uncertainty by continually reassessing our estimates of the natural rate and adjusting the stance of monetary policy accordingly.	13	1
201507	2730	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	So if the staff’s analysis of the survey evidence is correct, we’ll find that bringing inflation back to 2 percent requires a stronger labor market than we now anticipate.	13	1
201507	2731	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	As a result, I expect that, in response to incoming data, we’ll find ourselves raising the federal funds rate somewhat more slowly over time than we now expect.	13	1
201507	2732	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Like President Kocherlakota, a factor that I think is somewhat concerning is the decline over the past year in far-dated market-based measures of inflation compensation.	13	1
201507	2733	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	This decline, which has been partially reversed in the past few months, calls into question the premise that longer-run inflation expectations have remained stable over the past seven years and thus the forecast that inflation is headed back to pre-crisis levels.	13	1
201507	2734	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Fortunately, staff analysis suggests that most of the decline probably represents a shift in liquidity and inflation risk premiums rather than an actual fall in expectations per se.	13	1
201507	2735	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Accordingly, these data won’t lead me to raise serious questions about my inflation projection—particularly if they continue to drift back up toward their old level—but a renewed decline in inflation compensation would certainly give me pause.	13	1
201507	2736	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	The most important factor affecting my confidence will be the outlook for economic growth and the labor market.	13	1
201507	2737	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	I’ll need to see incoming data suggesting that real GDP growth will be enough above trend to complete the return to full employment even as interest rates rise.	13	1
201507	2738	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	If so, I likely will be reasonably confident that resource utilization will prove sufficiently tight to bring inflation back to 2 percent over the medium run.	13	1
201507	2739	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	But if the prospects for economic growth were to weaken in the near term, then I will be reluctant to begin the normalization process even if the cumulative improvement in labor market conditions has been appreciable.	13	1
201507	2740	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	As many of you noted, one recent favorable development for the outlook has been that the risks from the Greek debt situation have diminished, although Greece still faces a daunting path to debt sustainability.	13	1
201507	2741	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	But I, like several others, will be watching developments in China carefully because I judge the downside risks to be significant.	13	1
201507	2742	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	I’ll conclude by making two additional points about economic conditions and policy after the first increase in the funds rate.	13	1
201507	2743	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	First, I judge that, under appropriate policy, the unemployment rate probably needs to fall below its longer-run natural rate temporarily.	13	1
201507	2744	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	As I mentioned, like the staff, I judge that actual labor market slack currently exceeds the amount suggested by the unemployment gap.	13	1
201507	2745	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	I therefore think that an expeditious return to maximum employment will likely require the unemployment rate to undershoot my estimate of its longer- run normal level for a time in order to foster the tight conditions needed to bring labor force participation and involuntary part-time employment back to their normal, cyclically adjusted levels.	13	1
201507	2746	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Alternatively stated, the effective short-run natural rate, in my view, is lower than my assessment of the longer-run normal unemployment rate.	13	1
201507	2747	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	A period of somewhat tighter labor and product market conditions is also necessary to increase the likelihood that inflation will return to 2 percent at an acceptable pace.	13	1
201507	2748	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	This is a point illustrated by some of the Tealbook B simulations.	13	1
201507	2749	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Second, I’d note that it’s likely to be quite a while before the Committee can be fully confident of its outlook that inflation will return to our 2 percent objective.	13	1
201507	2750	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Based on the staff forecast, we will have to wait until early 2016 for the data to confirm that the inflation effects of lower oil prices and a higher dollar were, indeed, completely transitory.	13	1
201507	2751	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	It will take yet longer to confirm that inflation is moving back to 2 percent rather than just plateauing at around 1½ percent.	13	1
201507	2752	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	With verification of our basic inflation forecast likely to emerge so gradually, the normalization process will probably need to proceed quite cautiously.	13	1
201507	2753	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We may also want to explore alternatives to the “reasonably confident” language in our public statements, both at liftoff and beyond, to better indicate the uncertainty that we face.	13	1
201507	2754	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Let me stop there.	13	1
201507	2755	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We have a choice.	13	1
201507	2756	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Either we could ask Thomas to begin his monetary policy briefing now or we could quit and go have dinner.	13	1
201507	2757	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	How about we do the following.	13	1
201507	2758	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	I think we have plenty of time tomorrow morning.	13	1
201507	2759	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We’ll start off at 9:00 am  Thomas will begin his monetary policy briefing then.	13	1

201507	2772	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Thank you, Madam Chair.	21	2
201507	2773	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	I will be referring to the handout labeled “Material for Briefing on Monetary Policy Alternatives.”	21	2
201507	2774	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Your first exhibit reviews market participants’ monetary policy expectations and their economic conditionality.	21	2
201507	2775	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	The top two panels plot the probability distributions for the timing of liftoff derived from federal funds rate futures quotes—on the left— and responses to the Desk’s Survey of Primary Dealers—on the right—that Simon also showed in his briefing.	21	2
201507	2776	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Both show very low odds of policy firming at this meeting.	21	2
201507	2777	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	As Simon noted, some care needs to be taken in deriving probabilities from federal funds futures quotes to control for market participants’ assumptions about where in the target range the effective federal funds rate will trade.	21	2
201507	2778	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Under the assumption that it will trade in the middle of the range, the odds of liftoff in September based on federal funds futures are 33 percent; they are 40 percent, on average, in the dealer survey.	21	2
201507	2779	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Both show lower, but still significant, probabilities that policy normalization will begin in December, and, according to federal funds futures, there is roughly a 25 percent chance that it might begin only in March of next year or later.	21	2
201507	2780	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	As you can see from the dashed lines, investors’ views have changed little since the time of the June FOMC meeting.	21	2
201507	2781	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	The next three panels shed some light on investors’ views about the medium-term path for the federal funds rate as well as the economic forecasts that underlie these policy expectations.	21	2
201507	2782	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	As shown on the left, almost three-quarters of the primary dealers are anticipating that core PCE inflation during 2016 will be at or very close to 2 percent.	21	2
201507	2783	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	The expectation of the median respondent, shown by the blue vertical line, is close to that in the June SEP, shown by the black vertical line.	21	2
201507	2784	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	At the same time, as illustrated on the right, most dealers are anticipating that, by the end of next year, the unemployment rate will have fallen more noticeably below their estimates of the longer-run unemployment rate than was true for the SEP median.	21	2
201507	2785	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	The dots in the bottom-left panel show the paths of the federal funds rate associated with these economic projections.	21	2
201507	2786	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	The dealers’ expectation of a substantial tightening in resource utilization and of core inflation returning to close to 2 percent in 2016 seems consistent with the fact that most of them expect policy normalization to begin in September.	21	2
201507	2787	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	But although the median dealer expects labor markets to tighten somewhat faster than the median June SEP respondent, the median dealer’s projection of the federal funds rate is identical to the median SEP dot at the end of 2016 and slightly lower at the end of 2017.	21	2
201507	2788	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	This slightly lower path than in the SEP might reflect an expectation of a more accommodative policy stance or, alternatively, a lower path of the equilibrium real interest rate.	21	2
201507	2789	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	As shown in the lower-right panel, the primary dealers assign greater-than-even odds to the pace of tightening in the first year after liftoff being 100 basis points or less, and these expectations are essentially unchanged from June.	21	2
201507	2790	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Averaging across the Desk’s two surveys, the pace of tightening in the first two years following liftoff is about 100 basis points per year, conditioned on not returning to the zero lower bound.	21	2
201507	2791	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Returning to the lower-left panel, although the dealer survey traces an expected path for the federal funds rate not too different from the June SEP, the path derived from OIS quotes—the red line—runs substantially lower.	21	2
201507	2792	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	In part, this difference might reflect term premiums associated with the benefits of holding these nominal assets in states in which the federal funds rate remains very low.	21	2
201507	2793	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	While decomposing these risk-neutral expectations into term premiums and risk-adjusted expectations is challenging—especially with short-term rates at their effective lower bound—staff estimates suggest that only a modest share of the discrepancy between the OIS path and the other two paths can be explained by negative term premiums over the first two years.	21	2
201507	2794	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Thus, the marginal investors in this market seem to anticipate a yet more gradual pace of policy rate increases.	21	2
201507	2795	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	In sum, while market participants seem to be prepared for the possibility of policy tightening at your next meeting, they expect a lower trajectory of the federal funds rate over subsequent years than is embedded in the SEP median, after controlling for differences in their economic outlook to the extent we can.	21	2
201507	2796	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Turning to the draft statements for this meeting, the three alternatives offer a range of characterizations of current and prospective progress toward the Committee’s economic objectives and of the likelihood of policy tightening (or further policy tightening) at upcoming FOMC meetings.	21	2
201507	2797	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	As indicated in the bullets in the top panel of your second exhibit, alternative B is intended to convey the Committee’s assessment that the economy has been evolving in such a way that it could become appropriate to raise the target range for the federal funds rate in September, provided that the Committee sees additional progress toward maximum employment and becomes reasonably confident that inflation will move back to 2 percent over the medium term.	21	2
201507	2798	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	However, the language of the statement would express sufficient dependence on the incoming data to avoid deliberately shifting the current probability distribution of the timing of liftoff toward September and to retain the option to defer the start of normalization.	21	2
201507	2799	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	The message of paragraph 1 would be that the economy is again expanding moderately, with solid job gains and declining unemployment providing evidence of continued improvement in the labor market—one of your criteria for commencing normalization.	21	2
201507	2800	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	To underscore the Committee’s view of the importance of the cumulative progress in labor market conditions, paragraph 1 would note that “underutilization of labor resources has diminished since early this year.”	21	2
201507	2801	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Paragraph 3 would provide an additional indication that the Committee sees labor market conditions as having moved closer to those that would be consistent with policy normalization, saying that the Committee needs to see “some” further improvement in the labor market.	21	2
201507	2802	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative B would leave largely unchanged the Committee’s previously stated assessment of current and expected inflation developments and would repeat that it still needs to become reasonably confident that inflation will move back to 2 percent over the medium term.	21	2
201507	2803	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	However, the draft of paragraph 1 suggests dropping the reference to energy prices having stabilized.	21	2
201507	2804	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	The change would recognize that crude oil prices have fallen back a bit over the intermeeting period, and it could be read as suggesting that the drag on headline inflation from energy prices might not dissipate as quickly as previously anticipated.	21	2
201507	2805	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	As I indicated earlier, investors currently view September as the most likely meeting at which policy normalization will begin, and most dealers expect no material change to the forward guidance in today’s postmeeting statement.	21	2
201507	2806	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	That would seem to imply that a draft statement like alternative B would not elicit a significant market reaction or shift the probabilities of the timing of the first increase in the federal funds rate noticeably.	21	2
201507	2807	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	However, as we noted in Tealbook B, if market participants interpret the insertion of “some” in paragraph 3 as boosting the odds of a decision to raise the target range for the federal funds rate in September, then interest rates might rise, equity prices could fall, and the dollar would likely appreciate.	21	2
201507	2808	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	As noted in the middle panel, the draft statement for alternative A would provide an assessment of labor market conditions and inflation that would indicate that the Committee does not anticipate seeing, for some time, conditions that would warrant the beginning of policy normalization.	21	2
201507	2809	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Such a statement would likely shift the distribution of expectations regarding the date of policy tightening noticeably later.	21	2
201507	2810	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Paragraph 2 of alternative A would report that “in light of economic and financial developments abroad, the Committee sees the risks to the outlook for economic activity and the labor market as tilted to the downside.”	21	2
201507	2811	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	And it would indicate the Committee’s concern that “inflation could run substantially below the 2 percent objective for a protracted period.”	21	2
201507	2812	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	This concern would be emphasized by the introduction of a stronger inflation criterion for policy normalization in paragraph 3 and the addition of a commitment to use all of the Committee’s tools to return inflation to 2 percent within one to two years “if inflation does not begin to rise soon.”	21	2
201507	2813	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	The draft for alternative C—summarized in the lower panel—would present an assessment of economic conditions and the outlook consistent with a decision to raise the target range for the federal funds rate.	21	2
201507	2814	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	More important, it introduces for your consideration a number of other changes that you might make when you announce the start of policy normalization.	21	2
201507	2815	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	First, paragraph 2 would modify the reference to the policy assumption underlying the Committee’s outlook to indicate that it expects to continue to make “appropriate adjustments in the stance of monetary policy.”	21	2
201507	2816	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Paragraph 3 would set the stage for additional increases in the target range for the federal funds rate and would add a sentence emphasizing the Committee’s view that, “even after this adjustment, the stance of policy remains highly accommodative and will continue to support a strong economy.”	21	2
201507	2817	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	The new sentence would link the Committee’s assessment of the overall stance of policy directly to its principal policy tool—the funds rate.	21	2
201507	2818	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	In the current statement, that assessment only appears at the end of paragraph 4, in which the Committee states that keeping the balance sheet sizable “should help maintain accommodative financial conditions.”	21	2
201507	2819	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative C also provides several options for updating the forward guidance concerning future adjustments of the federal funds rate after normalization begins.	21	2
201507	2820	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	In paragraph 4, you might choose to follow the language of the Committee’s Statement on Longer-Run Goals and Monetary Policy Strategy and communicate that the Committee’s decisions will depend on its assessment of realized and expected “deviations from its objectives.”	21	2
201507	2821	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	However, if you are concerned that the reference to “deviations” would suggest that the Committee has a numerical definition of labor market conditions consistent with maximum employment, you may want to say more broadly that you will assess “economic conditions relative to” your objectives.	21	2
201507	2822	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	In either case, the draft offers an option of retaining the current guidance that the Committee “will take a balanced approach” to pursuing its objectives.	21	2
201507	2823	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	And, finally, while paragraph 4 would repeat the Committee’s expectation that “economic conditions may, for some time, warrant keeping the target federal funds rate below levels the Committee views as normal in the longer run,” it would also communicate that the Committee’s assessment might change as economic conditions evolve by stating that the actual path for the target range “will depend on the incoming data.”	21	2

201507	2826	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you very much.	23	2
201507	2827	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	To begin our go-round, I’d like to say just a few words about our policy decision and, in particular, our communications with the public.	23	2
201507	2828	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Economic conditions appear to be evolving in a manner that will likely make it appropriate to raise the target range for the federal funds rate sometime this year.	23	2
201507	2829	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	That was the message coming from the June SEP, and, based on what I heard during the economic go-round, I don’t believe that view has materially changed.	23	2
201507	2830	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	As was evident from my own remarks yesterday as well as from my own recent public communications, I believe that liftoff at our next meeting, in September, is a distinct possibility.	23	2
201507	2831	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	This decision, however, remains dependent on the data and their implications for the outlook.	23	2
201507	2832	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Hence, in our communications, we face the challenge of striking the right balance between keeping our options open, on the one hand, and not taking markets completely by surprise, on the other.	23	2
201507	2833	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Depending on how the data evolve and, along with them, both our thinking and that of the markets, achieving this balance may be tricky, and our public communications between now and liftoff will be under enormous scrutiny.	23	2
201507	2834	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	In considering this challenge, I went back and reviewed our policy on external communications, and I’m pleased that it offers some clear and useful guidance for us.	23	2
201507	2835	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	In particular, the first principle of our policy is that every Committee participant has an obligation to enhance the public’s understanding of monetary policy, including its rationale.	23	2
201507	2836	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	So I would ask you to try to keep this principle in mind at all times, but especially now, when there’s such tremendous focus on the timing of liftoff.	23	2
201507	2837	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	We have explicitly adopted a data-dependent approach to policy, and we’re not yet in a position to determine when we will raise rates.	23	2
201507	2838	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Opining in public on the exact timing of the first move, in my own view, not only detracts from our consensus-driven deliberative process, but also can easily confuse markets and the general public, adding to volatility and, ultimately, diminishing the effectiveness and credibility of our policy.	23	2
201507	2839	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	In addition, the more we talk about the precise timing of the first move, the more we stoke the media’s attention on one particular change in interest rates.	23	2
201507	2840	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	To be sure, the initial increase in the federal funds rate will be noteworthy, as it will mark the end of an extraordinary period of near-zero rates.	23	2
201507	2841	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	But, based on the economics, liftoff arguably contains more symbolism than substance.	23	2
201507	2842	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	As I’ve emphasized in my public statements, it is the entire expected path of the policy rate that matters for financial conditions in the economy, not just the initial increase.	23	2
201507	2843	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	And the real issue we will face is how cautiously we raise rates after liftoff to ensure that the economy can really absorb higher interest rates, and that inflation is truly heading back to 2 percent.	23	2
201507	2844	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, our communications guidelines affirm that participants are free to present their own views, but it’s critical that this be done in a way that clearly distinguishes one’s individual view from the Committee’s agreed-upon policy stance.	23	2
201507	2845	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	I would note that our policy explicitly prohibits making a prediction about Committee action in advance of the Committee announcement of its decision.	23	2
201507	2846	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	So my suggestion for all of us is to refrain from speculating about the time of liftoff.	23	2
201507	2847	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	One useful formulation when asked about liftoff is to say that no decisions have been made, the Committee remains focused on the data, and you look forward to discussing this decision with your colleagues at the next FOMC meeting.	23	2
201507	2848	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	If pressed, three additional points might be useful.	23	2
201507	2849	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	First, this can be seen from the June SEP.	23	2
201507	2850	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	If economic conditions evolve as expected, most FOMC participants view a first move sometime this year as likely.	23	2
201507	2851	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Second, even after the initial increase, policy will remain accommodative to support progress toward our dual objectives.	23	2
201507	2852	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	And, finally, as I just noted, it is the overall path of the policy rate that is of greatest import for the economy and not simply the first move.	23	2
201507	2853	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Let me end by noting that it’s conceivable to me that some type of communication may be warranted if we find ourselves in a situation in which the Committee appears inclined to raise the federal funds rate at our next meeting but markets, in the run-up, appear to be judging it as unlikely.	23	2
201507	2854	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	In that case, my inclination might be to make some widely available public comments through some sort of event or interview to try to better align public expectations for our near- term deliberations.	23	2
201507	2855	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	But I want to assure you that, before doing this, I would certainly consult with you to hear your thoughts and advice.	23	2
201507	2856	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Let me stop there, begin our go-round, and remind you that, in addition to your thoughts on today’s policy decision, it would be very useful if you could also provide your views regarding the suitability of alternative C for a meeting at which we first decide to raise the target range for the federal funds rate.	23	2

201507	2866	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I wasn’t sure what that was supposed to connote beyond what was already in paragraph 1.	22	2
201507	2867	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Paragraph 1 describes that labor markets have improved.	22	2
201507	2868	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We’re getting closer, presumably, to whatever represents maximum employment because of that progress.	22	2
201507	2869	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So I’m not sure what the word “some” was supposed to connote beyond what was already in paragraph 1.	22	2
201507	2870	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	My personal thinking is that it’s not unambiguous that “further improvement in the labor market” has a fixed starting point.	22	2
201507	2871	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	It could be simply measured in terms of further improvement from wherever you are today.	22	2
201507	2872	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	I think what the “some” signifies is simply that there is, in fact, implicit in this a fixed starting point, which was when the Committee first adopted this language, and that some of that distance has been traveled and only some of it remains.	22	2
201507	2873	2015-07-29	meeting	LAUBACH	That’s what it’s intended to clarify.	22	2
201507	2874	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Are there further questions for Thomas before we begin our go- round?	22	2

201507	2876	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota.	23	2
201507	2877	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you.	23	2
201507	2878	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Madam Chair, with the exception of a few months in late 2011 and early 2012, core PCE inflation has been below our adopted target of 2 percent for nearly seven years.	23	2
201507	2879	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The outlook in Tealbook A is that it will not return to target until the next decade.	23	2
201507	2880	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I do not see this outcome as consistent with our commitment to keep inflation at 2 percent over the longer run.	23	2
201507	2881	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	How can we do better?	23	2
201507	2882	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The staff provides a clear answer to this question in the excellent optimal control simulations in Tealbook B, in which they put zero weight on unemployment falling below the natural rate.	23	2
201507	2883	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Basically, we can facilitate a more rapid return of inflation to target if we are not averse to living in an America in which the unemployment rate is below 5 percent for several years.	23	2
201507	2884	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, for those of us in the Ninth District, we can tell you it’s not so bad to have unemployment below 5 percent.	23	2
201507	2885	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We live with it all the time.	23	2
201507	2886	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So if we’re willing to make policy choices that give rise to unemployment rates in the 4s for an extended period of time, then those policy choices will push inflation back to target in a much more timely fashion.	23	2
201507	2887	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, the optimal control exercises also indicate that we could obtain those outcomes, even if we initiate liftoff later this year rather than waiting longer, as long as we raise the federal funds rate very slowly, by about 10 basis points per quarter.	23	2
201507	2888	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But I’m not convinced this “go early and super slowly” approach is the best one.	23	2
201507	2889	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	A key part of what makes these policies work in the simulations is, the agents in the model know that the FOMC is not averse to having unemployment below 5 percent.	23	2
201507	2890	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the real world, the public doesn’t know that, and I don’t believe that lifting off in, say, September would signal that clearly.	23	2
201507	2891	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	From this communications point of view, we would be much better off deferring liftoff until, say, the latter portion of next year and then raising the federal funds rate more rapidly than 10 basis points per quarter.	23	2
201507	2892	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As the footnotes in Tealbook B suggest, we would get pretty similar inflation and unemployment outcomes by doing that—as long as assumptions in the model are met, of course.	23	2
201507	2893	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	All of this is based on the modal outlook.	23	2
201507	2894	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I talked yesterday about some of the downside risks—possibly adverse international outcomes and a further downward slide in inflation expectations.	23	2
201507	2895	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I thought Governor Brainard’s comments on the dollar were ones that really sharpen the points I was attempting to make about international risks.	23	2
201507	2896	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Especially in light of the constraints imposed by the zero lower bound, these risks also support deferring liftoff until we have a stronger inflation outlook.	23	2
201507	2897	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am sure that some of you, perhaps many of you, are undoubtedly concerned about other risks:  a possibility that the Phillips curve may prove to be considerably steeper than what the staff has modeled, or that risks to financial stability arise from low interest rates.	23	2
201507	2898	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These are absolutely legitimate concerns.	23	2
201507	2899	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Committee meets eight times per year and gets plenty of advance warning for these particular outcomes.	23	2
201507	2900	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We’ll hear about and see inflationary pressures through the behavior of inflation itself and through our intelligence- gathering efforts.	23	2
201507	2901	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The QS report, through the diligent work of our staff, will reveal risks to financial stability.	23	2
201507	2902	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we feel that the QS report is not designed to elicit the kinds of risks to financial stability that we’re concerned about, we should be letting our staff know what other information they should, in fact, be including in that report.	23	2
201507	2903	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Importantly, not only do we get the information about these risks when they actually materialize, but this Committee also has the tools to deal with these risks, should they transpire.	23	2
201507	2904	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It can increase rates more rapidly; it can halt reinvestments sooner; and it can, if needed, sell assets.	23	2
201507	2905	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is in contrast with the downward risks, concerning which we’re so constrained by the zero lower bound.	23	2
201507	2906	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Madam Chair, I urge the Committee to be willing to pursue our 2 percent inflation objective with urgency, even if that pursuit results in an unemployment rate under 5 percent for an extended period of time.	23	2
201507	2907	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So I recommend alternative A.	23	2
201507	2908	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	While I’m recommending alternative A, I do have a comment about alternative B, which follows up on the question I asked Thomas.	23	2
201507	2909	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I would suggest not including the word “some” in paragraph 3.	23	2
201507	2910	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think that a good discipline on all communication is, we should be adding words if we have a very specific message we want to deliver.	23	2
201507	2911	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m not sure what message the Committee is attempting to deliver.	23	2
201507	2912	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If the Committee is attempting to deliver the message that September is very “live” in its thinking, the route you were describing whereby you were going to have a public set of remarks during the intermeeting period seemed like a much more useful way to proceed.	23	2
201507	2913	2015-07-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201507	2914	2015-07-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2

201507	2917	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I support alternative B.	23	2
201507	2918	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Between now and the September meeting, we will have two employment reports and further evidence on whether we are experiencing wage and price acceleration consistent with returning PCE inflation to 2 percent in the medium term.	23	2
201507	2919	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While I’m reasonably confident that labor markets will continue to improve, particularly in light of the apparent waning of several important geopolitical concerns, I need to see more data to determine whether we are returning to our 2 percent inflation target within a reasonable horizon.	23	2
201507	2920	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Although the oil price decline and dollar appreciation since the end of last year are likely to be attenuating, recent movements in oil prices and the exchange rate indicate that these forces may be continuing to influence pricing developments.	23	2

201507	2923	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	My own view is that, in September, core PCE inflation may be as likely to fall further as to rise—not probabilities consistent with reasonable confidence of a return to target.	23	2
201507	2924	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The economy is approaching a point at which the Committee will confront a difficult decision at each meeting.	23	2
201507	2925	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If labor markets continue to improve and the wage and price data show further evidence of inflation returning to target, I could be persuaded that September was the time for liftoff.	23	2
201507	2926	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, I can easily imagine that wage and price data will not be improving as hoped, and that a later liftoff would be appropriate.	23	2
201507	2927	2015-07-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The statement is data dependent, and I believe we should be open minded to reacting only when the data have confirmed the conditions we have set out in our statement.	23	2
